Commentary Notes
intermediate
8 min
The Quran's Critique of Blind Ancestral Following
Author critiques blind ancestral following using Quranic verses on deities and conjecture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic argument against blind taqlid and explain why it is epistemologically invalid.

Core Idea
The Qur'an condemns following ancestors without evidence as following conjecture and desire.

In this lesson, we examine how the Qur'an liberates reason by exposing the error of blindly adhering to ancestral traditions. The author presents several verses that mock those who prefer ancestral ways over divine revelation, and he highlights that such adherence is based on conjecture (zann) and desire (hawa), not on certain knowledge. We will analyze the logical structure of this critique and understand why it is a foundational epistemological principle in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ancestral tendency criticized
Find the verses where people say they follow their fathers. Notice the Quran's response: it asks if following ancestors is valid even if ancestors were misguided.
2
Extract the epistemological basis of the critique
The author notes that the Quran attacks false deities by name, showing they have no authority. The polytheists' only justification is 'we found our fathers doing this.' Identify the logical fallacy: appealing to tradition as evidence.
3
Analyze the role of conjecture and desire
The verse in Surah an-Najm says they follow only assumption (zann) and what their souls desire (hawa). Contrast this with the guidance (huda) from Allah. What makes zann an unreliable source?
4
Recognize the Quranic denial of power to false gods
Verses like 39:43 and 46:5-6 show that false gods cannot intercede or respond. The author argues that worshipping them is irrational because they lack ability. How does this reinforce the critique of ancestral authority?

وفي سياقات أخرى كثيرة يذم القرآن الكريم النزعة الآبائية، جاهداً ويسعى خلال تسفيه معتقدات الآباء و موروثاتهم المختلفة - إلى تحرير العقل من سطوة تفكير السلطات ومراكزها وإيقاظه ابتغاء معاودة نشاطه وفاعليته، ومما جاء في هذا: ﴿وَإِذا قِيلَ لَهُمُ اتَّبِعُوا مَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ قَالُوا بَلْ نَتَّبِعُ مَا وَجَدْنَا عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَنَا أَوَلَوْ كانَ الشَّيْطَانُ يَدْعُوهُمْ إِلَى عَذَابِ السَّعِيرِ﴾ [لقمان: ٢١/٣١]. ﴿بَلْ قالُوا إِنَّا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا عَلَى أُمَّةٍ وَإِنَّا عَلَى آثَارِهِمْ مُهْتَدُونَ، وَكَذَلِكَ ما أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ قَبْلِكَ فِي قَرْيَةٍ مِنْ نَذِيرٍ إِلَّا قَالَ مُتْرَفُوهَا إِنَّا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا عَلَى أُمَّةٍ وَإِنَّا عَلَى آثَارِهِمْ مُقْتَدُونَ، قَالَ أَوَلَوْ جِئْتُكُمْ بِأَهْدَى مِمَّا وَجَدْتُمْ عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَكُمْ قَالُوا إِنَّا بِما أُرْسِلْتُمْ بِهِ كَافِرُونَ﴾ [الزخرف: ٢٢/٤٣-٢٤]. ﴿إِنَّهُمْ أَلْقَوْا آبَاءَهُمْ ضَالَّينَ، فَهُمْ عَلَى آثَارِهِمْ يُهْرَعُونَ﴾ [الصافات: ٦٩/٣٧-٧٠]. ويشن حملة عنيفة على معبوداتهم بأسمائها، حيث لا مستند لشرعيتها إلا وصف الآباء لها، هذا إلى جانب اتباعهم الظن والهوى، مع أن مصدر الهداية قائم في القرآن الكريم ﴿أَفَرَأَيْتُمُ اللآت وَالْعُزَّى، وَمَناةَ الثَّالِثَةَ الأُخْرَى، أَلَكُمُ الذَّكَرُ وَلَهُ الأُنثى، تِلْكَ إِذَا قِسْمَةٌ ضِيزَى إِنْ هِيَ إِلا أَسْمَاءً سَمَّيْتُمُوهَا أَنْتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ ما أَنْزَلَ الله بها مِنْ سُلطان إِنْ يَبعُونَ إِلا الظَّنَّ وَما تَهْوَى الْأَنْفُسُ وَلَقَدْ جَاءَهُمْ مِنْ رَبِّهِمُ الْهُدَى﴾ [النجم: ١٩/٥٣-٢٣]. ويؤكد القرآن نفيه الصريح لأي قدرة مادية أو عقلية لدى معبوداتهم تلك، فكيف تستقيم هذه العبادة مع أن فاقد الشيء لا يعطيه: ﴿وَمَا اتَّخَذُوا مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ شُفَعاءَ قُلْ أَوَلَوْ كَانُوا لا يَمْلِكُونَ شَيْئًا وَلَا يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [الزمر: ٤٣/٣٩]. وفي موضع آخر: ﴿وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنْ يَدْعُو مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مَنْ لا يَسْتَجِيبُ لَهُ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَهُمْ عَنْ دُعَائِهِمْ غَافِلُونَ، وَإِذا حُشِرَ النَّاسُ كَانُوا لَهُمْ أَعْدَاءً وَكَانُوا بعِبادَتِهِمْ كَافِرِينَ﴾ [الأحقاف: ٥/٤٦-٦]. وفي سبيل تحرير العقل من سلطان الآباء والعشيرة يورد القرآن المنهج الإبراهيمي، القائم على أسلوب الحوار العقلي، لكشف ما هم عليه من ضلال: ﴿وَاتْلُ عَلَيْهِمْ نَبَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِذْ قالَ لأَبِيهِ وَقَوْمِهِ مَا تَعْبُدُونَ، قَالُوا نَعْبُدُ أَصْناماً فَنَظَلُّ لَها عاكِفِينَ، قَالَ هَلْ يَسْمَعُونَكُمْ إِذْ تَدْعُونَ، أَوْ يَنْفَعُونَكُمْ أَوْ يَضُرُّونَ قَالُوا بَلْ وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا كَذَلِكَ يَفْعَلُونَ، قَالَ أَفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْبُدُونَ، أَنتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمُ الأَقْدَمُونَ، فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوٌّ لِي إِلا رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ الَّذِي خَلَقَنِي فَهُوَ يَهْدِينِ، وَالَّذِي هُوَ يُطْعِمُنِي وَيَسْقِينِ، وَإِذا مَرِضْتُ فَهُوَ يَشْفِينِ، وَالَّذِي يُمِيتُي ثُمَّ يُحْيِينِ، وَالَّذِي أَطْمَعُ أَنْ يَغْفِرَ لِي خَطِيئَتِي يَوْمَ الدِّينِ﴾ [الشعراء: ٦٩/٢٦-٨٢]. ﴿وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ رُشْدَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَكُنَا بِهِ عَالِمِينَ، إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ وَقَوْمِهِ ما هَذِهِ التِّمَاثِيلُ الَّتِي أَنْتُمْ لَها عاكِفُونَ قَالُوا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا لَها عابِدِينَ، قَالَ لَقَدْ كُنتُمْ أَنتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينِ، قَالُوا أَجِئْتَنا بِالْحَقِّ أَمْ أَنْتَ مِنَ اللَّاعِبِينَ، قَالَ بَلْ رَبُّكُمْ رَبُّ السَّماواتِ وَالأَرْضِ الَّذِي فَطَرَهُنَّ وَأَنا عَلَى ذَلِكُمْ مِنَ الشَّاهِدِينَ، وتاللَّهِ لأَكِيدَنَّ أَصْنَامَكُمْ بَعْدَ أَنْ تُوَلُّوا مُدْبِرِينَ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٥١/٢١-٥٧]. وصفوة القول أن الإنسان حين يلغي مصدر معرفته العقلية وأدواتها، ويعيش عالة على ما خلّفه الآباء من ميراث - على أهمية ميراث الآباء فيما يتصل بالمعرفة التراكمية – فإن ذلك يغدو تحولاً إلى آصار وأغلال للعقل.
And in many other contexts, the noble Qur'an condemns the ancestral tendency, striving through discrediting the beliefs of the fathers and their various inheritances to liberate the intellect from the dominance of the thinking of authorities and centers, and to awaken it seeking to renew its activity and effectiveness. Among what is mentioned in this: [Quran 31:21] 'And when it is said to them, Follow what Allah has revealed, they say, Rather, we follow that upon which we found our fathers. Even if Satan was inviting them to the punishment of the Blaze?' [Quran 43:22-24] 'Rather, they say, Indeed, we found our fathers upon a religion, and we are, in their footsteps, guided. And similarly, We did not send before you any warner into a city except that its affluent said, Indeed, we found our fathers upon a religion, and we are, in their footsteps, following. [The warner] said, Even if I brought you better guidance than that upon which you found your fathers? They said, Indeed, we, in that with which you were sent, are disbelievers.' [Quran 37:69-70] 'Indeed they found their fathers astray, so they hasten in their footsteps.' And he launches a fierce campaign against their deities by name, where there is no basis for their legitimacy except the description of the fathers for them, besides their following assumption and desire, while the source of guidance is established in the noble Qur'an: [Quran 53:19-23] 'So have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza and Manat, the third, the other? Is the male for you and for Him the female? That, then, is an unjust division. They are but names you have named, you and your fathers, for which Allah sent down no authority. They follow not except assumption and what the souls desire, and there has come to them from their Lord guidance.' And the Qur'an affirms its clear denial of any material or intellectual ability of those deities, so how can this worship be correct with the principle that one who lacks something cannot give it: [Quran 39:43] 'Or have they taken besides Allah intercessors? Say, Even though they do not possess anything and do not reason?' And in another place: [Quran 46:5-6] 'And who is more astray than one who invokes besides Allah one who will not respond to him until the Day of Resurrection, and they, of their invocation, are unaware. And when the people are gathered, they will be enemies to them and will deny their worship.' And in order to liberate the intellect from the authority of fathers and tribe, the Qur'an presents the Abrahamic methodology, based on the style of rational dialogue, to uncover the misguidance they are upon: [Quran 26:69-82] 'And recite to them the news of Abraham, when he said to his father and his people, What do you worship? They said, We worship idols and we remain to them devoted. He said, Do they hear you when you supplicate? Or do they benefit you or harm? They said, Rather, we found our fathers doing thus. He said, Then do you see what you have been worshipping, you and your ancient forefathers? Indeed, they are enemies to me, except the Lord of the worlds, who created me, and He guides me, and who feeds me and gives me drink, and when I am ill, He heals me, and who causes me to die and then gives me life, and who I hope will forgive me my sin on the Day of Recompense.' [Quran 21:51-57] 'And We had certainly given Abraham his sound judgment before, and We were of him well-knowing. When he said to his father and his people, What are these statues to which you are devoted? They said, We found our fathers worshippers of them. He said, You have certainly been, you and your fathers, in manifest error. They said, Have you come to us with truth, or are you of those who jest? He said, Rather, your Lord is the Lord of the heavens and the earth who created them, and I, to that, am of the witnesses. And by Allah, I will surely plan against your idols after you turn your backs.' In summary, when a person abolishes his source of rational knowledge and its tools, and lives dependent on the inheritance left by fathers – despite the importance of paternal inheritance with regard to cumulative knowledge – that becomes a transformation into fetters and shackles for the intellect.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique of blind adherence to ancestral tradition (taqlid) and a defense of the Qur'an's methodology in liberating human reason. The author begins by stating that the Qur'an condemns the 'ancestral tendency' and aims to free the intellect from the dominance of authoritative thinking. He then cites several Quranic verses that expose the fallacy of following ancestors without evidence. In Surah Luqman (31:21), the Qur'an mocks those who prefer ancestral ways over divine revelation, even if their ancestors were misguided. Similarly, Surah az-Zukhruf (43:22-24) highlights that affluent leaders of previous nations rejected prophets because they clung to ancestral religion, regardless of superior guidance. The author then notes Surah as-Saffat (37:69-70), where the disbelievers are described as blindly rushing after their astray fathers. The Qur'an also attacks the polytheistic deities themselves, pointing out that they are mere names with no authority, and that the polytheists follow only conjecture and desire (Surah an-Najm 53:19-23). The author emphasizes that the Qur'an denies any power to these false gods, asking how worship can be valid when they lack both material and intellectual capacity (Surah az-Zumar 39:43; Surah al-Ahqaf 46:5-6). To further illustrate the liberation of reason, the author presents the example of Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham), who used rational dialogue to challenge his father and people. In Surah ash-Shu'ara (26:69-82), Ibrahim asks what they worship, and when they reply they follow their ancestors, he counters by asking whether the idols can hear, benefit, or harm. He then declares that those idols are his enemies, affirming his worship of Allah alone, who creates, guides, feeds, heals, and forgives. In Surah al-Anbiya (21:51-57), Ibrahim directly calls his people's worship of statues based on ancestral tradition a 'manifest error' and demonstrates his commitment to the truth. The author concludes that abolishing intellectual tools and living solely on ancestral heritage, while acknowledging its value for cumulative knowledge, turns the intellect into chains and fetters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the epistemological problem with following ancestors as the polytheists did?
A) They followed ancestors who were ignorant
B) They followed ancestors without evidence, relying on conjecture and desire
C) They followed ancestors who were not scholars
D) They followed ancestors from a different religion

Key Takeaway
Blindly following ancestral tradition without evidence is a logical fallacy and an epistemological error that the Qur'an systematically refutes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Use the Quranic verses from this lesson to construct a short argument against someone who says 'I only follow what my parents and grandparents believed, and that is enough for me.' Point out the logical fallacy and the Quranic response.
?
Task 2: In a fiqh discussion, a student claims that a certain ruling must be correct because 'the early scholars all agreed on it.' Is this an appeal to tradition? How would you distinguish between valid reliance on scholarly consensus (ijma') and blind taqlid? Write a brief response.

Commentary Notes
intermediate
8 min
The Abrahamic Method of Rational Dialogue
Author presents Ibrahim's rational dialogue as a model for freeing reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the steps of Prophet Ibrahim's rational dialogue and analyze how it serves as a model for liberating reason from ancestral authority.

Core Idea
Prophet Ibrahim uses rational questions to expose the nullity of idolatry and affirm tawhid.

Having presented the Quran's general critique of ancestral authority, the author now turns to the example of Prophet Ibrahim as the paradigm of rational inquiry. Ibrahim does not simply reject his people's beliefs; he engages them in dialogue, asking critical questions about the idols' ability to hear, benefit, or harm. This lesson will walk through the verses and extract the logical method Ibrahim employs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the setting of Ibrahim's dialogue
Read the verses from Surah ash-Shu'ara (26:69-82) and Surah al-Anbiya (21:51-57). Who is Ibrahim addressing? What is the context?
2
Extract Ibrahim's first line of questioning
He asks: 'What do you worship?' and then 'Do they hear you? Do they benefit or harm you?' What is the logical purpose of these questions?
3
Analyze the response of the people
They reply: 'We found our fathers doing so.' Notice this is the same appeal to tradition criticized earlier. Ibrahim then exposes that the idols are useless.
4
Examine Ibrahim's positive declaration
He affirms the worship of Allah alone, describing His attributes (creates, guides, feeds, heals, etc.). How does this rational declaration serve as a contrast to the idols?
5
Recognize Ibrahim's decisive action
In Surah al-Anbiya, he declares his plan to destroy the idols. How does this follow from the rational dialogue?

وفي سياقات أخرى كثيرة يذم القرآن الكريم النزعة الآبائية، جاهداً ويسعى خلال تسفيه معتقدات الآباء و موروثاتهم المختلفة - إلى تحرير العقل من سطوة تفكير السلطات ومراكزها وإيقاظه ابتغاء معاودة نشاطه وفاعليته، ومما جاء في هذا: ﴿وَإِذا قِيلَ لَهُمُ اتَّبِعُوا مَا أَنْزَلَ اللهُ قَالُوا بَلْ نَتَّبِعُ مَا وَجَدْنَا عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَنَا أَوَلَوْ كانَ الشَّيْطَانُ يَدْعُوهُمْ إِلَى عَذَابِ السَّعِيرِ﴾ [لقمان: ٢١/٣١]. ﴿بَلْ قالُوا إِنَّا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا عَلَى أُمَّةٍ وَإِنَّا عَلَى آثَارِهِمْ مُهْتَدُونَ، وَكَذَلِكَ ما أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ قَبْلِكَ فِي قَرْيَةٍ مِنْ نَذِيرٍ إِلَّا قَالَ مُتْرَفُوهَا إِنَّا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا عَلَى أُمَّةٍ وَإِنَّا عَلَى آثَارِهِمْ مُقْتَدُونَ، قَالَ أَوَلَوْ جِئْتُكُمْ بِأَهْدَى مِمَّا وَجَدْتُمْ عَلَيْهِ آبَاءَكُمْ قَالُوا إِنَّا بِما أُرْسِلْتُمْ بِهِ كَافِرُونَ﴾ [الزخرف: ٢٢/٤٣-٢٤]. ﴿إِنَّهُمْ أَلْقَوْا آبَاءَهُمْ ضَالَّينَ، فَهُمْ عَلَى آثَارِهِمْ يُهْرَعُونَ﴾ [الصافات: ٦٩/٣٧-٧٠]. ويشن حملة عنيفة على معبوداتهم بأسمائها، حيث لا مستند لشرعيتها إلا وصف الآباء لها، هذا إلى جانب اتباعهم الظن والهوى، مع أن مصدر الهداية قائم في القرآن الكريم ﴿أَفَرَأَيْتُمُ اللآت وَالْعُزَّى، وَمَناةَ الثَّالِثَةَ الأُخْرَى، أَلَكُمُ الذَّكَرُ وَلَهُ الأُنثى، تِلْكَ إِذَا قِسْمَةٌ ضِيزَى إِنْ هِيَ إِلا أَسْمَاءً سَمَّيْتُمُوهَا أَنْتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ ما أَنْزَلَ الله بها مِنْ سُلطان إِنْ يَبعُونَ إِلا الظَّنَّ وَما تَهْوَى الْأَنْفُسُ وَلَقَدْ جَاءَهُمْ مِنْ رَبِّهِمُ الْهُدَى﴾ [النجم: ١٩/٥٣-٢٣]. ويؤكد القرآن نفيه الصريح لأي قدرة مادية أو عقلية لدى معبوداتهم تلك، فكيف تستقيم هذه العبادة مع أن فاقد الشيء لا يعطيه: ﴿وَمَا اتَّخَذُوا مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ شُفَعاءَ قُلْ أَوَلَوْ كَانُوا لا يَمْلِكُونَ شَيْئًا وَلَا يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [الزمر: ٤٣/٣٩]. وفي موضع آخر: ﴿وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنْ يَدْعُو مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مَنْ لا يَسْتَجِيبُ لَهُ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَهُمْ عَنْ دُعَائِهِمْ غَافِلُونَ، وَإِذا حُشِرَ النَّاسُ كَانُوا لَهُمْ أَعْدَاءً وَكَانُوا بعِبادَتِهِمْ كَافِرِينَ﴾ [الأحقاف: ٥/٤٦-٦]. وفي سبيل تحرير العقل من سلطان الآباء والعشيرة يورد القرآن المنهج الإبراهيمي، القائم على أسلوب الحوار العقلي، لكشف ما هم عليه من ضلال: ﴿وَاتْلُ عَلَيْهِمْ نَبَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِذْ قالَ لأَبِيهِ وَقَوْمِهِ مَا تَعْبُدُونَ، قَالُوا نَعْبُدُ أَصْناماً فَنَظَلُّ لَها عاكِفِينَ، قَالَ هَلْ يَسْمَعُونَكُمْ إِذْ تَدْعُونَ، أَوْ يَنْفَعُونَكُمْ أَوْ يَضُرُّونَ قَالُوا بَلْ وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا كَذَلِكَ يَفْعَلُونَ، قَالَ أَفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْبُدُونَ، أَنتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمُ الأَقْدَمُونَ، فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوٌّ لِي إِلا رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ الَّذِي خَلَقَنِي فَهُوَ يَهْدِينِ، وَالَّذِي هُوَ يُطْعِمُنِي وَيَسْقِينِ، وَإِذا مَرِضْتُ فَهُوَ يَشْفِينِ، وَالَّذِي يُمِيتُي ثُمَّ يُحْيِينِ، وَالَّذِي أَطْمَعُ أَنْ يَغْفِرَ لِي خَطِيئَتِي يَوْمَ الدِّينِ﴾ [الشعراء: ٦٩/٢٦-٨٢]. ﴿وَلَقَدْ آتَيْنَا إِبْرَاهِيمَ رُشْدَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَكُنَا بِهِ عَالِمِينَ، إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ وَقَوْمِهِ ما هَذِهِ التِّمَاثِيلُ الَّتِي أَنْتُمْ لَها عاكِفُونَ قَالُوا وَجَدْنَا آبَاءَنَا لَها عابِدِينَ، قَالَ لَقَدْ كُنتُمْ أَنتُمْ وَآبَاؤُكُمْ فِي ضَلالٍ مُبِينِ، قَالُوا أَجِئْتَنا بِالْحَقِّ أَمْ أَنْتَ مِنَ اللَّاعِبِينَ، قَالَ بَلْ رَبُّكُمْ رَبُّ السَّماواتِ وَالأَرْضِ الَّذِي فَطَرَهُنَّ وَأَنا عَلَى ذَلِكُمْ مِنَ الشَّاهِدِينَ، وتاللَّهِ لأَكِيدَنَّ أَصْنَامَكُمْ بَعْدَ أَنْ تُوَلُّوا مُدْبِرِينَ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٥١/٢١-٥٧]. وصفوة القول أن الإنسان حين يلغي مصدر معرفته العقلية وأدواتها، ويعيش عالة على ما خلّفه الآباء من ميراث - على أهمية ميراث الآباء فيما يتصل بالمعرفة التراكمية – فإن ذلك يغدو تحولاً إلى آصار وأغلال للعقل.
And in many other contexts, the noble Qur'an condemns the ancestral tendency, striving through discrediting the beliefs of the fathers and their various inheritances to liberate the intellect from the dominance of the thinking of authorities and centers, and to awaken it seeking to renew its activity and effectiveness. Among what is mentioned in this: [Quran 31:21] 'And when it is said to them, Follow what Allah has revealed, they say, Rather, we follow that upon which we found our fathers. Even if Satan was inviting them to the punishment of the Blaze?' [Quran 43:22-24] 'Rather, they say, Indeed, we found our fathers upon a religion, and we are, in their footsteps, guided. And similarly, We did not send before you any warner into a city except that its affluent said, Indeed, we found our fathers upon a religion, and we are, in their footsteps, following. [The warner] said, Even if I brought you better guidance than that upon which you found your fathers? They said, Indeed, we, in that with which you were sent, are disbelievers.' [Quran 37:69-70] 'Indeed they found their fathers astray, so they hasten in their footsteps.' And he launches a fierce campaign against their deities by name, where there is no basis for their legitimacy except the description of the fathers for them, besides their following assumption and desire, while the source of guidance is established in the noble Qur'an: [Quran 53:19-23] 'So have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza and Manat, the third, the other? Is the male for you and for Him the female? That, then, is an unjust division. They are but names you have named, you and your fathers, for which Allah sent down no authority. They follow not except assumption and what the souls desire, and there has come to them from their Lord guidance.' And the Qur'an affirms its clear denial of any material or intellectual ability of those deities, so how can this worship be correct with the principle that one who lacks something cannot give it: [Quran 39:43] 'Or have they taken besides Allah intercessors? Say, Even though they do not possess anything and do not reason?' And in another place: [Quran 46:5-6] 'And who is more astray than one who invokes besides Allah one who will not respond to him until the Day of Resurrection, and they, of their invocation, are unaware. And when the people are gathered, they will be enemies to them and will deny their worship.' And in order to liberate the intellect from the authority of fathers and tribe, the Qur'an presents the Abrahamic methodology, based on the style of rational dialogue, to uncover the misguidance they are upon: [Quran 26:69-82] 'And recite to them the news of Abraham, when he said to his father and his people, What do you worship? They said, We worship idols and we remain to them devoted. He said, Do they hear you when you supplicate? Or do they benefit you or harm? They said, Rather, we found our fathers doing thus. He said, Then do you see what you have been worshipping, you and your ancient forefathers? Indeed, they are enemies to me, except the Lord of the worlds, who created me, and He guides me, and who feeds me and gives me drink, and when I am ill, He heals me, and who causes me to die and then gives me life, and who I hope will forgive me my sin on the Day of Recompense.' [Quran 21:51-57] 'And We had certainly given Abraham his sound judgment before, and We were of him well-knowing. When he said to his father and his people, What are these statues to which you are devoted? They said, We found our fathers worshippers of them. He said, You have certainly been, you and your fathers, in manifest error. They said, Have you come to us with truth, or are you of those who jest? He said, Rather, your Lord is the Lord of the heavens and the earth who created them, and I, to that, am of the witnesses. And by Allah, I will surely plan against your idols after you turn your backs.' In summary, when a person abolishes his source of rational knowledge and its tools, and lives dependent on the inheritance left by fathers – despite the importance of paternal inheritance with regard to cumulative knowledge – that becomes a transformation into fetters and shackles for the intellect.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique of blind adherence to ancestral tradition (taqlid) and a defense of the Qur'an's methodology in liberating human reason. The author begins by stating that the Qur'an condemns the 'ancestral tendency' and aims to free the intellect from the dominance of authoritative thinking. He then cites several Quranic verses that expose the fallacy of following ancestors without evidence. In Surah Luqman (31:21), the Qur'an mocks those who prefer ancestral ways over divine revelation, even if their ancestors were misguided. Similarly, Surah az-Zukhruf (43:22-24) highlights that affluent leaders of previous nations rejected prophets because they clung to ancestral religion, regardless of superior guidance. The author then notes Surah as-Saffat (37:69-70), where the disbelievers are described as blindly rushing after their astray fathers. The Qur'an also attacks the polytheistic deities themselves, pointing out that they are mere names with no authority, and that the polytheists follow only conjecture and desire (Surah an-Najm 53:19-23). The author emphasizes that the Qur'an denies any power to these false gods, asking how worship can be valid when they lack both material and intellectual capacity (Surah az-Zumar 39:43; Surah al-Ahqaf 46:5-6). To further illustrate the liberation of reason, the author presents the example of Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham), who used rational dialogue to challenge his father and people. In Surah ash-Shu'ara (26:69-82), Ibrahim asks what they worship, and when they reply they follow their ancestors, he counters by asking whether the idols can hear, benefit, or harm. He then declares that those idols are his enemies, affirming his worship of Allah alone, who creates, guides, feeds, heals, and forgives. In Surah al-Anbiya (21:51-57), Ibrahim directly calls his people's worship of statues based on ancestral tradition a 'manifest error' and demonstrates his commitment to the truth. The author concludes that abolishing intellectual tools and living solely on ancestral heritage, while acknowledging its value for cumulative knowledge, turns the intellect into chains and fetters.

Key Terms
المنهج الإبراهيمي
الحوار العقلي
البرهان
الضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the people's response when Ibrahim asked them why they worship idols?
A) They said they found their fathers doing so
B) They admitted they were ignorant
C) They challenged Ibrahim's authority
D) They converted immediately

Key Takeaway
Prophet Ibrahim's use of rational dialogue demonstrates that ancestral tradition is not a valid justification for belief; beliefs must be based on evidence and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Imagine you are in a discussion with someone who worships a saint and justifies it by saying 'my ancestors did this.' Using Ibrahim's method, what questions would you ask to expose the lack of evidence? Write a short dialogue.
?
Task 2: Compare Ibrahim's method in these verses to the method used by a mutakallim in a debate. How does the rational approach of 'asking questions' help in establishing truth?

The Quran's Command to Use Intellect
Author cites Quranic verses to establish the necessity of intellect in understanding revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic verses that command intellectual engagement and explain how they support the organic unity of intellect and revelation.

Core Idea
The Quran itself commands reflection, understanding, and pondering.

This lesson examines the first part of the passage, where the author cites several Quranic verses that explicitly call for intellectual activities like tafakkur (reflection), tadabbur (pondering), and ta'qil (understanding). These verses are not incidental; they form the basis for the author's claim that intellect is integral to Islam and that there is an organic unity between divine rulings and reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic commands
Locate the verses cited in the passage: An-Nahl 16:44, Al-Isra 17:41, Yusuf 12:2, and An-Nisa 4:82. For each verse, note the specific intellectual act mentioned (e.g., reflection, reminder, understanding, pondering).
2
Extract the author's inference
After citing the verses, the author draws a conclusion: 'This indicates that an aspect of doctrinal and legislative rulings is inseparable from the intellect.' Identify this claim and understand how the verses serve as evidence for it.
The author uses the Quranic invitations to reason as proof that intellect is not foreign to revelation.
3
Understand the organic unity
The author asserts 'no contradiction, but rather cooperation and mutual support' between intellect and Islam. Paraphrase this relationship in your own words, showing how the verses demonstrate that intellect is required to properly engage with the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالْبَيِّنَاتِ وَالزُّبُرِ وَأَنْزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الذِّكْرَ لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِّلَ إِلَيْهِمْ وَلَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَفَكَّرُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٤/١٦]. ﴿وَلَقَدْ صَرَّفْنَا فِي هَذَا الْقُرْآنِ لِيَذْكُرُوا ﴾ [الإسراء: ٤١/١٧]. إنا أَنزَلْنَاهُ قُرْآناً عَرَبِيًّا لَعَلَّكُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [يوسف: ٢/١٢]. أَفَلا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْآن وَلَوْ كانَ مِنْ عِندِ غَيْرِ اللَّهِ لَوَجَدُوا فِيهِ اخْتِلافاً كثيراً) [النساء: ٨٢/٤). إن هذا يشير إلى أن جانباً من الأحكام العقدية والتشريعية لا ينفصل عن العقل، بما يؤكد الوحدة العضوية بين منظومة أحكام الإسلام وبين العقل، وأن لا تعارض بينهما، بل تضافر ومؤازرة. ٦- العقل والنبوة: وثمة دعوة إلى إعمال العقل للتأكد من صدق نبوة محمد -صلى الله عليه وسلم- ورسالته: أَوَلَمْ يَتَفَكَّرُوا ما بِصاحِبِهِمْ مِنْ جِنَّةِ إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا نَذِيرٌ مُبِينٌ ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٨٤/٧]. وقُلْ لا أَقُولُ لَكُمْ عِنْدِي خَزَائِنُ اللهِ وَلا أَعْلَمُ الْغَيْبَ وَلَا أَقُولُ لَكُمْ إِنِّي مَلَكَ إِن أَتَّبِعُ إِلَّا مَا يُوحَى إِلَيَّ قُلْ هَلْ يَسْتَوِي الأَعْمَى وَالْبَصِيرُ أَفَلا تَتَفَكَّرُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٥٠/٦]. وهذا يعني أن النبوة لا تعني إلغاء للعقل كما أن العقل لا يستغني عن النبوة، وتلك ركيزة هامة أخرى من ركائز التربية الإسلامية.
With clear proofs and scriptures, and We sent down to you the Reminder that you may explain to the people what was revealed to them, and that perhaps they will reflect. [An-Nahl 16:44] And We have certainly diversified in this Quran that they may be reminded. [Al-Isra 17:41] Indeed, We sent it down as an Arabic Quran so that you might understand. [Yusuf 12:2] Then do they not reflect upon the Quran? If it had been from other than Allah, they would have found within it much contradiction. [An-Nisa 4:82] This indicates that an aspect of doctrinal and legislative rulings is inseparable from the intellect, affirming the organic unity between the system of Islamic rulings and the intellect, and that there is no contradiction between them, but rather cooperation and mutual support. 6- Intellect and Prophethood: There is also an invitation to employ the intellect to verify the truth of Muhammad's prophethood and message: Do they not reflect that their companion is not possessed? He is only a clear warner. [Al-A'raf 7:184] And Say, 'I do not say to you that I have the treasures of Allah, nor do I know the unseen, nor do I say to you that I am an angel. I only follow what is revealed to me.' Say, 'Are the blind and the seeing equal? Then will you not give thought?' [Al-An'am 6:50] This means that prophethood does not entail the abolition of the intellect, just as the intellect cannot dispense with prophethood. That is another important pillar of Islamic education.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage establishes the complementary relationship between intellect and revelation. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that explicitly call for reflection (tafakkur), reminder (tadhakkur), understanding (ta'qil), and pondering (tadabbur) of the Quran. These verses show that the Quran itself demands intellectual engagement. The author then draws a key conclusion: doctrinal and legal rulings are inseparable from the intellect, meaning there is an organic unity, not a contradiction, between Islam and reason. Next, the author introduces a specific application: verifying the truth of Muhammad's prophethood. Verses are cited that ask the disbelievers to reflect on the character of the Prophet (that he is not mad) and to compare the blind and the seeing (ignorance and knowledge). The author concludes that prophethood does not cancel the intellect, and the intellect cannot be self-sufficient without revelation. This mutual interdependence is a fundamental principle of Islamic education.

Key Terms
العقل
التفكر
التدبر
التذكر
التعقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the Quranic verses calling for intellectual activities indicate?
A) The intellect is irrelevant to understanding revelation.
B) The intellect and revelation are in constant conflict.
C) There is an organic unity between intellect and Islam.
D) The Quran forbids using the intellect for doctrinal matters.

Key Takeaway
The Quran repeatedly commands intellectual engagement, showing that intellect is integral to understanding revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Write a short paragraph explaining how the verse 'Then do they not reflect upon the Quran?' (An-Nisa 4:82) supports the idea that the Quran invites rational scrutiny. Use the author's conclusion about organic unity in your explanation.

Verifying Prophethood Through Intellect
Author argues that the Quran commands using intellect to verify prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct an argument from the Quran that the intellect is used to confirm the truth of prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophethood does not abolish the intellect; the intellect verifies prophethood.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage, where the author addresses the specific use of intellect to verify the prophethood of Muhammad (SAW). By citing Al-A'raf 7:184 and Al-An'am 6:50, the author shows that the Quran invites rational examination of the Prophet’s character and message, concluding that prophethood and intellect are complementary, not contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses on verification
Find the verses Al-A'raf 7:184 and Al-An'am 6:50 in the passage. Note what each verse asks: the first asks if they reflect that the Prophet is not possessed; the second contrasts the blind and seeing and ends with 'will you not give thought?'
2
Distinguish the author's conclusion
The author concludes: 'This means that prophethood does not entail the abolition of the intellect, just as the intellect cannot dispense with prophethood.' Identify this as the main claim and see how the verses provide evidence for it.
The verses show that the Quran itself encourages rational evaluation of prophethood's claims.
3
Recognize the mutual interdependence
The author says prophethood does not cancel intellect, nor can intellect be self-sufficient without revelation. Paraphrase this relationship, understanding that both are needed: intellect to verify and understand prophethood, and prophethood to guide the intellect beyond its limits.

Intellect and Prioritizing the Hereafter
Quranic call to compare world and Hereafter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Quran uses the intellect to compare the value of this world and the Hereafter and construct an argument for prioritizing the Hereafter.

Core Idea
The intellect distinguishes amusement from ultimate reality.

The Quran does not merely command belief; it invites the intellect to compare the fleeting nature of this world with the permanent Hereafter. In this lesson, we see how the verse 'So will you not use reason?' (Qasas 28:60) is a direct appeal to rational comparison.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two entities compared
Locate the verses 29:64 and 28:60 in the passage. What are the two things being contrasted? (worldly life vs. Hereafter)
2
Extract the attributes assigned
Note that worldly life is described as 'amusement and play' and 'commodity and adornment'; the Hereafter is 'true life' and 'better and more lasting'.
The Arabic terms: لهو ولعب, متاع وزينة, الحيوان, خير وأبقى.
3
Recognize the intellect's role
The verse 'So will you not use reason?' directly asks the intellect to weigh these attributes and choose the superior.
The intellect is not passive; it is called to actively compare and conclude.
4
Understand the educational insight
The author explains that intellectual education helps strengthen faith in the unseen and matures a person beyond childish short-term interests.
This rational comparison is an educational tool to elevate the believer's perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العقل لمعرفة حقيقة الدنيا والآخرة: ﴿وَمَا هَذِهِ الْحَيَاةُ الدُّنْيَا إِلا لَهْوٌ وَلَعِبٌ وَإِنَّ الدَّارَ الْآخِرَةَ لَهِيَ الْحَيَوَانُ لَوْ كَانُوا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٦٤/٢٩]. ﴿وَمَا أُوتِيتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَمَتَاعُ الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَزِينَتُهَا وَمَا عِنْدَ اللهِ خَيْرٌ وَأَبْقَى أَفَلا تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [القصص: ٦٠/٢٨]. ومن الناحية التربوية فإن التربية العقلية تمثل عاملاً مساعداً في تعزيز الإيمان بالغيب عن طريق الوحي، كما تسهم في إخراج الإنسان المؤمن الذي لا يقف عند حدود الاهتمامات القريبة، التي قد تكون مناسبة لعالم الطفولة، الذي يسوغ فيه الفرح بالألعاب، ولكنه لا يناسب الإنسان الراشد، صاحب الاهتمامات الكبيرة، وصاحب النظرة الآفاقية، كما أن في هذه الآيات إرشاداً إلى الجمع بين الوسائل والغايات وإلى مرحلة الغايات والأهداف، وذلك من صلب اهتمامات النظام التربوي، والعمل التعليمي في المؤسسات التربوية. العقل وقصص السابقين: ودعا القرآن إلى إعمال العقل وأخذ العبرة من قصص السابقين، كما جاء ذلك عقب ذكر قصة لوط - على سبيل المثال - ﴿وَلَقَدْ تَرَكْنَا مِنْهَا آيَةً بَيِّنَةً لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٣٥/٢٩]. وفي ذلك تربية على التعلم بالعبرة، بوصفها أسلوباً تربوياً معتبراً في تدريس التربية الإسلامية. - الحث على الفقه الكوني: والفقه الكوني يمثل جماع الوظائف العقلية وأعمقها: ﴿قُلْ هُوَ الْقَادِرُ عَلَى أَنْ يَبْعَثَ عَلَيْكُمْ عَذَاباً مِنْ فَوْقِكُمْ أَوْ مِنْ تَحْتِ أَرْجُلِكُمْ أَوْ يَلْبِسَكُمْ شِيَعًا وَيُذِيقَ بَعْضَكُمْ بَأْسَ بَعْضٍ انْظُرْ كَيْفَ نُصَرِّفُ الآياتِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦٥/٦]
The intellect for understanding the reality of this world and the Hereafter: And this worldly life is not but amusement and play; but indeed, the home of the Hereafter is the true life, if they but knew. [Ankabut 29:64] And whatever thing you have been given is but a commodity of the worldly life and its adornment; but what is with Allah is better and more lasting. So will you not use reason? [Qasas 28:60] From an educational perspective, intellectual education represents a factor that helps strengthen faith in the unseen through revelation, and it contributes to producing a believing person who does not limit himself to short-term interests, which may be appropriate for the world of childhood where amusement with play is permissible, but it is not suitable for the mature person, the one of great concerns and broad vision. Also, these verses guide to combining means and ends and focusing on the stage of ends and goals—this is core to the concerns of the educational system and instructional work in educational institutions. Intellect and the stories of predecessors: The Quran called for employing the intellect and taking lessons from the stories of predecessors, as it came after the story of Lot—for example—And We left therein a clear sign for a people who use reason. [Ankabut 29:35] That is education by learning from examples, as a valid educational method in teaching Islamic education. Encouragement of cosmic understanding: Cosmic understanding represents the sum and deepest of intellectual functions: Say, 'He is able to send upon you punishment from above you or from beneath your feet, or to confuse you into sects and make you taste the violence of one another.' Look how We diversify the verses that they might understand. [An'am 6:65]
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of the intellect's role in the Quran. It is divided into three sub-points. First, the author cites verses that contrast the fleeting nature of this world with the eternal Hereafter, using the intellect to recognize the superior value of the Hereafter. The author then provides an educational insight: intellectual training helps strengthen faith in the unseen (al-ghayb) through revelation, and it matures a person beyond childish short-term concerns to a broader, eternal perspective. Second, the author brings up the Quran's use of stories of past nations, citing the example of Lot, and emphasizes that the intellect should derive lessons (al-ibra) from these stories. This is presented as a pedagogical method in Islamic education. Third, the author introduces the concept of 'cosmic understanding' (al-fiqh al-kawni), which is the deepest intellectual function. A verse is quoted that shows Allah's power over people's fate, and the aim of diversifying signs is for people to understand (yafqahun). The author implies that the intellect is essential to comprehend the universe and derive signs of divine power.

Key Terms
العقل
الحياة الدنيا
الآخرة
لَهْو وَلَعِب
مَتَاع
زِينَة
خَيْر وَأَبْقَى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main function of the intellect in relation to the two verses quoted?
A) To reject worldly life completely
B) To compare the fleeting nature of this world with the permanence of the Hereafter and choose the superior
C) To prove the existence of God
D) To understand scientific phenomena

Key Takeaway
The Quran calls the intellect to compare the transient world with the eternal Hereafter, strengthening faith in the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the verse 'The mutual rivalry for piling up the good things of this world diverts you' (Takathur 102:1) and compare it with 'So will you not use reason?' from Qasas 28:60. How does the Quran use the intellect to shift attention from competition in this world to the Hereafter?

Commentary Notes
beginner
5 min
Intellect and Learning from Stories of Predecessors
Quranic call to derive lessons from history

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Quran uses historical stories as a means for intellectual reflection (al-ibra) and apply this method to Islamic education.

Core Idea
History is a classroom for the intellect.

The Quran repeatedly narrates stories of past nations and commands us to take lessons. In this lesson, we see the example of the story of Lot, where the Quran says 'We left therein a clear sign for a people who use reason.' The intellect is the tool to extract a lesson from history.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Quranic example
Find the verse about the story of Lot (Ankabut 29:35) in the passage. What does the Quran say about the sign left after that nation?
2
Understand the term 'ibra'
The author defines 'al-ibra' as a lesson derived from historical events. Why is this an intellectual act?
The verse says 'for a people who use reason' (li qawmin ya'qilun), linking intellect with taking lessons.
3
Recognize the educational method
The author states that this is 'education by learning from examples' (al-ta'allum bil-ibra). How does this method work in Islamic education?
It is a pedagogical approach that uses past events to teach moral and spiritual lessons.
4
Apply to a different story
Think of another Quranic story (e.g., Pharaoh, 'Ad, Thamud). How would you use the intellect to derive a lesson from it?
The lesson might be about arrogance, gratitude, or the consequences of rejecting prophets.

intermediate

Cosmic Understanding as the Deepest Intellectual Function
Encouragement of cosmic understanding as deep reflection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain what cosmic understanding (al-fiqh al-kawni) is and how the Quran encourages it as the deepest intellectual function.

Core Idea
Observing the universe is an intellectual act of worship.

The Quran not only calls to reflect on history but also on the natural world. In this lesson, we examine 'cosmic understanding' (al-fiqh al-kawni), which the author describes as the sum and deepest of intellectual functions. The verse from Surah al-An'am shows that understanding Allah's signs in the universe requires deep reflection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term 'al-fiqh al-kawni'
Find where the author introduces 'cosmic understanding'. What does he say about its status?
It is 'the sum and deepest of intellectual functions' (جماع الوظائف العقلية وأعمقها).
2
Analyze the quoted verse
Read An'am 6:65. What phenomena are described? (punishment from above/below, sects). The verse ends with 'that they might understand' (yafqahun). What is the connection?
Diversifying signs is for deep understanding.
3
Understand the role of the intellect
The intellect is needed to perceive the signs in natural and historical events as signs of Allah's power and wisdom.
This goes beyond surface observation; it is a deep comprehension of the universe as a text of divine signs.
4
Apply to a natural phenomenon
Think of a natural phenomenon like rain or the alternation of day and night. How would cosmic understanding approach it?
For example, rain is not just a physical process but a sign of Allah's mercy and power, as in Quran 30:48-50.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العقل لمعرفة حقيقة الدنيا والآخرة: ﴿وَمَا هَذِهِ الْحَيَاةُ الدُّنْيَا إِلا لَهْوٌ وَلَعِبٌ وَإِنَّ الدَّارَ الْآخِرَةَ لَهِيَ الْحَيَوَانُ لَوْ كَانُوا يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٦٤/٢٩]. ﴿وَمَا أُوتِيتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَمَتَاعُ الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَزِينَتُهَا وَمَا عِنْدَ اللهِ خَيْرٌ وَأَبْقَى أَفَلا تَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [القصص: ٦٠/٢٨]. ومن الناحية التربوية فإن التربية العقلية تمثل عاملاً مساعداً في تعزيز الإيمان بالغيب عن طريق الوحي، كما تسهم في إخراج الإنسان المؤمن الذي لا يقف عند حدود الاهتمامات القريبة، التي قد تكون مناسبة لعالم الطفولة، الذي يسوغ فيه الفرح بالألعاب، ولكنه لا يناسب الإنسان الراشد، صاحب الاهتمامات الكبيرة، وصاحب النظرة الآفاقية، كما أن في هذه الآيات إرشاداً إلى الجمع بين الوسائل والغايات وإلى مرحلة الغايات والأهداف، وذلك من صلب اهتمامات النظام التربوي، والعمل التعليمي في المؤسسات التربوية. العقل وقصص السابقين: ودعا القرآن إلى إعمال العقل وأخذ العبرة من قصص السابقين، كما جاء ذلك عقب ذكر قصة لوط - على سبيل المثال - ﴿وَلَقَدْ تَرَكْنَا مِنْهَا آيَةً بَيِّنَةً لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٣٥/٢٩]. وفي ذلك تربية على التعلم بالعبرة، بوصفها أسلوباً تربوياً معتبراً في تدريس التربية الإسلامية. - الحث على الفقه الكوني: والفقه الكوني يمثل جماع الوظائف العقلية وأعمقها: ﴿قُلْ هُوَ الْقَادِرُ عَلَى أَنْ يَبْعَثَ عَلَيْكُمْ عَذَاباً مِنْ فَوْقِكُمْ أَوْ مِنْ تَحْتِ أَرْجُلِكُمْ أَوْ يَلْبِسَكُمْ شِيَعًا وَيُذِيقَ بَعْضَكُمْ بَأْسَ بَعْضٍ انْظُرْ كَيْفَ نُصَرِّفُ الآياتِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَفْقَهُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٦٥/٦]

According to the passage, what does cosmic understanding (al-fiqh al-kawni) represent?
A) A minor intellectual function
B) The sum and deepest of intellectual functions

?

Identify specific natural phenomena mentioned and explain how the intellect uses them to arrive at cosmic understanding (al-fiqh al-kawni).

Commentary Notes
intermediate
5 min
Linking Quranic 'Nasiya' to the Frontal Lobes
Author links modern anatomical studies of the brain's frontal lobes to the Quranic mention of 'al-nasiya'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the neuroscientific claim about 'al-nasiya' and assess its relationship to the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
The Quranic forelock may point to the frontal lobes, the seat of higher cognition and moral action.

This lesson examines a contemporary claim that the Quran's mention of 'al-nasiya' (forelock) refers specifically to the brain's frontal lobes, based on modern neuroscience. We'll analyze how the author connects anatomical findings to the Quranic text and consider the logical structure of this claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the anatomical region
Locate the description of brain areas in the text. Which area is highlighted as the center for higher mental functions?
The author mentions the frontal association area in the anterior part of the frontal lobes.
2
Find the Quranic parallel
Find where the author equates that brain region with 'al-nasiya' and quote the verse. What is the context of the verse?
The verse threatens a lying, sinful forelock.
3
Analyze the connection
How does the author justify identifying the frontal lobes with 'nasiya'? Is it based on location, function, or both?
The author notes that the frontal lobes are at the front of the head and responsible for higher functions like thinking and speech.
4
Evaluate the claim
Consider whether this claim is a logical deduction or an assertion. What assumptions are made about the Quranic term?
The claim assumes that 'nasiya' in the verse refers to a specific anatomical structure, not just a metaphorical forelock.

وقد توصلت الدراسات التشريحية الحديثة إلى تحديد مناطق معينة في لحاء المخ مهمتها القيام بوظائف سيكولوجية محددة. ولعل أهم هذه المناطق المنطقة الحركية المسيطرة على حركة أجزاء الجسم جميعاً، والمنطقة الحسية التي تنتهي إليها إحساسات اللمس، والمنطقة البصرية، والمنطقة السمعية ومنطقة الترابط الجبهية الموجودة في معظم الجزء الأمامي من الفصين الجبهيين، وتمثل مركزاً للعمليات العقلية العليا، كالتعلم والتفكير والقراءة والكتابة والكلام. إن هذه المنطقة - منطقة الفصين الجبهيين - تكون في مقدم الرأس من لحاء المخ، وتسمى (الناصية) وهي المذكورة في قول الله تعالى: {كَلَّا لَئِنْ لَمْ يَنتَهِ لَنَسْفَعاً بِالنَّاصِيَةِ، نَاصِيَةٍ كاذبة خاطئة} [العلق: 96/15-16]. فالقول الكاذب أو الفعل الخاطئ المشار إليه في الآية الكريمة يبدأ أولاً في خلايا
And modern anatomical studies have identified specific areas in the cerebral cortex that perform specific psychological functions. Perhaps the most important of these areas are: the motor area controlling movement of all body parts, the sensory area where touch sensations end, the visual area, the auditory area, and the frontal association area located in most of the anterior part of the frontal lobes, representing a center for higher mental operations such as learning, thinking, reading, writing, and speech. Commentary
This passage connects modern neuroscience with a Quranic verse. The author reports that anatomical studies have mapped brain regions, notably the frontal association area in the frontal lobes, which is responsible for higher mental functions like learning, thinking, reading, writing, and speech. This area is located in the front part of the brain's cortex and is identified as 'al-nasiya' (the forelock) mentioned in Quran 96:15-16, where God threatens to drag the sinner by the forelock. The author then implies that false speech or sin originates in the cells of this area, linking physical brain function to moral behavior. This is a form of scientific commentary on the Quran.

Attention (Tanabbuh) as a Gateway to Knowledge
Author defines attention and its role in learning, citing Quranic commands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of attention in learning from an Islamic epistemological perspective, citing Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Attention is the gateway to knowledge; without it, even revelation cannot be received.

This lesson explores the concept of attention (tanabbuh) as a fundamental cognitive process for acquiring knowledge. The author connects modern psychological insights with Quranic commands to listen attentively, establishing attention as a prerequisite for learning and spiritual success.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of attention in the passage
Identify how the author defines tanabbuh: as a high mental process involving focused awareness, essential for learning and comprehension.
The passage uses both tanabbuh and intibāh synonymously.
2
Recognize the psychological role of attention in learning
Note the example: if a person does not pay attention to a lecture, they cannot perceive, learn, or retrieve the information. Attention is thus a prerequisite for effective learning.
3
Identify the Quranic evidence
Locate the two verses cited: Quran 7:204 commands listening attentively during Quran recitation, and Qaf 50:37 mentions 'giving ear while witnessing' as a condition for receiving admonition.
The second verse follows warnings about destroyed nations, linking inattention to spiritual loss.
4
Connect attention to spiritual consequences
Understand that inattention leads not only to poor learning but also to missing divine guidance, as shown by the context of destroyed nations.
5
Apply to teaching Islamic education
The author concludes that attention is a valuable method for Islamic education, so teachers must actively arouse students' attention for effective comprehension.

أولاً: التنبه
من المقرر عند علماء النفس أن للانتباه دوراً هاماً في عملية التعلم واكتساب المعرفة وتحصيل العلم. فعدم الانتباه إلى محاضرة ما يجعل المستمع غير قادر على إدراك ما تضمنته من المعلومات، ومن ثم فلن يتمكن من تعلمها أو استرجاعها فيما بعد. ولذلك كان عامل الانتباه لدى المعلمين في إثارة انتباه تلاميذهم على غاية الأهمية في عملية استيعاب الدرس وتحصيله. وهذا ما أشار إليـه القرآن بقوله: ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْآنُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنْصِتُوا لَعَلَّكُمْ تُرْحَمُونَ﴾ [الأعراف: ٢٠٤/٧]. وإنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَى لِمَنْ كانَ لَهُ قَلْبٌ أَوْ أَلْقَى السَّمْعَ وَهُوَ شَهِيدٌ [rv/o.:3]. ومن الجدير ذكره أن هذه الآية الأخيرة وردت عقب ذكر هلاك أمم كثيرة من الكفار قبل قريش (۳).
والتنبه بوصفه أسلوباً عقلياً راقياً يعد أحد الأساليب الجديرة باعتمادها ضمن طرائق تدريس التربية الإسلامية.
First: Attention. It is established among psychologists that attention plays an important role in the process of learning, acquiring knowledge, and attaining science. So, lack of attention to a lecture makes the listener unable to perceive the information it contains, and then he will not be able to learn it or retrieve it later. Therefore, the factor of attention among teachers in arousing the attention of their students is of utmost importance in the process of comprehending and attaining the lesson. This is what the Quran indicated with His saying: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy' [Al-A'raf 7:204]. And indeed in that is a reminder for whoever has a heart or gives ear while witnessing. And it is worth mentioning that this last verse came after the mention of the destruction of many nations of disbelievers before Quraysh. And attention as a high mental method is one of the methods worthy of being adopted among the teaching methods of Islamic education.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition on the role of attention (tanabbuh) in learning. The author begins by stating the established psychological finding that attention is crucial for learning, acquiring knowledge, and attaining science. He illustrates this with a practical example: if a person does not pay attention to a lecture, they cannot grasp the information or later recall it. Therefore, teachers must prioritize arousing students' attention for effective comprehension. The author then supports this with Quranic evidence, quoting Surah Al-A'raf 7:204, which commands attentive listening during Quran recitation. He notes that this verse follows a warning about destroyed nations, implying that inattention leads to spiritual loss. Finally, he concludes that attention, as a high-level mental method, is valuable for teaching Islamic education.

Key Terms
التنبه (al-tanabbuh): A high mental process involving focused awareness, essential for learning and comprehension, as described in this passage.
الانتباه (al-intibāh): Used synonymously with tanabbuh; the act of directing one's attention to a stimulus, critical for knowledge acquisition.

Attention is not passive; it is an active, high-level mental process essential for learning and for truly receiving divine guidance.

Al-Ghazali's Critique of Causal Necessity
Author presents al-Ghazali's argument against necessary causality and compares it to Western empiricism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Ghazali's argument against necessary causality and identify its epistemological basis in Ash'ari theology.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali denies necessary causality, asserting only habitual conjunction created by God.

This lesson delves into al-Ghazali's famous critique of causal necessity, a cornerstone of Ash'ari theology. You will work through his argument from the Tahafut, where he systematically dismantles the philosophers' claim that cause and effect are linked by logical necessity. The goal is to understand not just what al-Ghazali said, but why his argument matters for Islamic epistemology and how it parallels—and differs from—later Western empiricism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of al-Ghazali's critique
Read the passage from 'Al-Ghazali considered the claim...' to the end. What specific doctrine is he attacking? He targets the philosophers' assertion that the relation between cause and effect is necessary and that breaking habits (kharq al-ʿādāt) is impossible.
The philosophers here refer to the falāsifa, particularly Ibn Sīnā.
2
Extract al-Ghazali's core claim
Find the sentence where al-Ghazali states his position directly: 'The conjunction between what is habitually believed to be a cause and what is habitually believed to be an effect is not necessary in our view.' This is the thesis.
The Arabic phrase is 'al-iqtirān... laysa ḍarūriyyan ʿindanā'.
3
Analyze the examples used
Al-Ghazali lists pairs like drinking and quenching, fire and burning, beheading and death. For each, he argues that God could create one without the other. Identify how each example illustrates the denial of necessary connection.
Note that these examples are all from everyday experience, not abstract.
4
Understand the theological basis
Al-Ghazali invokes God's prior decree (taqdīr) and creation 'on concomitance' (ʿalā al-tasāwuq). This reflects the Ash'ari doctrine that God directly creates every event, and regularities are God's habit (ʿāda), not necessary laws.
This is not a denial of regularity, only of necessity.
5
Compare with the Western empiricists
The author compares al-Ghazali to Hume and others. Note that whereas Hume bases his critique on sensory experience and psychology, al-Ghazali bases his on divine omnipotence and occasionalism.
This comparison is not part of al-Ghazali's original text but is added by the commentator.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل

التجارب التي أمكن الحصول عليها). وهذا يعني أن التجربة الحسية يعوزها تطبيق هذه المبادئ، ولا تنفك ملازمة لها، ومن غير المتصوّر إمكان استقلال الحس وحده من غير استناد إليها. فالتجربة عقلية - إذن - لقيامها على قوانين العقل الأولية. وفي ذلك تأكيد على أن الاختبار القبلي من شأن العقل، أما الاختبار البعدي فيرجع إلى الحس، بما يومئ إلى ضرورة تضافرهما معاً. وإذا كان مرد الخلاف بين وجهتي النظر سواء القائلة بانتماء السببية إلى العقل أو تلك القائلة بانتمائه إلى الحس إنما هو النزاع بين المذهبين العقلي والحسي، فإن النزاع في الفكر الإسلامي اتخذ منحى آخر. إذ تصدرت فرقة الأشاعرة لتبني اتجاه نفي السببية، وزعمت عدم وجود ضرورة في العلاقة بين العلة والمعلول، أو السبب والمسبب، وعدّت ما قد يظهر من تلازم بينهما مجرد اقتران بين شيئين، أو اطراد بين حادثتين، دون أن يكون لأحدهما أثر على الأخرى، بل الأمر مجرد تجاور عادي.

إن هذا التفسير شبيه بتفسير الاتجاه التجريبي الذي تبلور بعد ذلك في الغرب، وتبناه أمثال لوك (Lock) و مالبرانش (Malebranche) وهيوم (Hume) وبركلي (Berkelly)، ثم تابعهم أغلب الوضعيين وفي مقدمتهم المؤسس الأول: أوجست كونت (Ogust Cont) الذي رفض الميتافيزيقا لأنها غير خاضعة للتجربة، والاشتغال بها ـ عنده ـ يمثل لغواً، لقد شبهها (كونت) بألعاب الحواة أي التهريج. كما سفه (هيوم) فكرة السببية من أساسها.

ويشير أحد الباحثين إلى أن (هيوم) قد واجه فكرة السببية من الأساس بما يفوق نفي الغزالي لها. في حين يرى (رينان) أن (هيوم) ما زاد شيئاً أكثر مما تكلمه الغزالي وسبق إليه.

لقد عد الغزالي القول بضرورة السببية من أباطيل الفلاسفة. ونراه يفند المتصلة بهذا المبدأ فيقول في (تهافت الفلاسفة): المقولة السابعة عشرة : في إبطال قولهم في استحالة خرق العادات الاقتران بين ما يعتقد في العادة سبباً وبين ما يعتقد مسبباً ليس ضرورياً عندنا، بل كل شيئين ليس هذا ذاك، ولا ذاك هذا، ولا إثبات أحدهما متضمناً لإثبات الآخر، ولا نفيه متضمناً لنفي الآخر فليس من ضرورة وجود أحدهما وجود الآخر، ولا من ضرورة عدم أحدهما عدم الآخر، مثل الري والشرب والشبع و الأكل، والاحتراق ولقاء النار، والنور وطلوع الشمس والموت وجز الرقبة والشفاء وشرب الدواء، وإسهال البطن واستعمال المسهل، وهلم جراً إلى كل المشاهدات من المقترنات في الطب والنجوم والصناعات والحرف فإن اقترانها لما سبق من تقدير الله سبحانه – بخلقها على التساوق لا لكونه ضرورياً في نفسه، غير قابل للفرق، بل في المقدور خلق الشبع دون الأكل، وخلق الموت دون جز الرقبة، وإدامة الحياة مع جز الرقبة، وهلم جراً إلى المقترنات. وأنكر الفلاسفة إمكانه وادعوا استحالة.

والنظر في هذه الأمور الخارجة عن الحصر يطول فلنعين مثالاً واحداً وهو الاحتراق في القطن عند ملاقاة النار، فإننا نجوّز وقوع الملاقاة بينهما دون الاحتراق، ونجوّز حدوث انقلاب القطن رماداً محترقاً دون ملاقاة النار، وهم ينكرون جوازه.
Chapter Three: Section Two - The Intellect

Experiments that could be obtained). This means that sensory experience lacks the application of these principles, and it is not separate from them, and it is inconceivable that the senses alone could be independent without relying on them. Thus experience is intellectual - therefore - because it is based on the primary laws of the intellect. This confirms that a priori testing is the concern of the intellect, while a posteriori testing returns to the senses, indicating the necessity of their collaboration. And if the point of disagreement between the two viewpoints, whether claiming that causality belongs to the intellect or claiming that it belongs to the senses, is the conflict between the rationalist and empiricist schools, then the conflict in Islamic thought took another direction. For the Ash'ari school took the lead in adopting the direction of denying causality, claiming that there is no necessity in the relationship between cause and effect, or cause and caused, and they considered what may appear as correlation between them as mere conjunction between two things, or regularity between two events, without one having any effect on the other, rather it is merely ordinary juxtaposition.

This interpretation is similar to the empiricist trend that later developed in the West, adopted by the likes of Locke, Malebranche, Hume, and Berkeley, followed by most positivists, foremost among them the first founder: Auguste Comte, who rejected metaphysics because it is not subject to experience, and occupying oneself with it - in his view - is nonsense; he likened it (Comte) to the games of jugglers, i.e., buffoonery. Hume also disparaged the idea of causality from its foundation.

One researcher points out that Hume confronted the idea of causality from its foundation in a way that surpasses al-Ghazali's negation of it. While Renan holds that Hume added nothing more than what al-Ghazali had said and anticipated.

Al-Ghazali considered the claim of the necessity of causality to be among the falsehoods of the philosophers. We see him refuting those connected with this principle in his 'Tahafut al-Falasifa': The Seventeenth Discussion: On invalidating their claim about the impossibility of breaking habits. The conjunction between what is habitually believed to be a cause and what is habitually believed to be an effect is not necessary in our view. Rather, any two things where this is not that, nor that this, nor does affirming one entail affirming the other, nor does denying it entail denying the other, it is not necessary that the existence of one implies the existence of the other, nor that the non-existence of one implies the non-existence of the other. Examples: quenching and drinking, satiety and eating, burning and contact with fire, light and sunrise, death and beheading, recovery and drinking medicine, purging of the stomach and using a laxative, and so on to all observed conjunctions in medicine, astronomy, crafts, and trades. Their conjunction is due to God's prior decree - by creating them in concomitance, not because it is necessary in itself, incapable of separation. Rather, it is within [divine] power to create satiety without eating, to create death without beheading, to sustain life despite beheading, and so on to all conjunctions. The philosophers denied its possibility and claimed it is impossible.

Examining these countless matters would be lengthy, so let us cite one example: the burning of cotton upon contact with fire. For we deem it possible that contact occurs between them without burning, and we deem it possible that the cotton turns into burned ashes without contact with fire, while they deny its permissibility.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the Ash'ari denial of necessary causality, focusing on al-Ghazali's famous argument from his 'Tahafut al-Falasifa'. The author begins by situating the debate within the broader conflict between rationalist and empiricist epistemologies, noting that Islamic thought took a distinct turn with the Ash'ari school, which denied any necessary connection between cause and effect, viewing observed regularities as mere conjunction (iqṭirān) decreed by God. The author then draws parallels to Western empiricists like Hume and Berkeley, and notes the debate over whether Hume surpassed or merely repeated al-Ghazali. The core of the lesson is the lengthy quote from al-Ghazali, where he systematically argues that the link between what we habitually call cause and effect is not logically necessary. He provides examples from everyday life—eating and satiety, fire and burning, beheading and death—to illustrate that God could create the effect without the cause or vice versa. Al-Ghazali emphasizes that the philosophers' claim of impossibility is unfounded; the conjunction is due to God's habitual practice ('āda), not inherent necessity. The passage concludes with the specific example of cotton burning: al-Ghazali affirms that God could prevent burning despite contact with fire, or create burning without contact, whereas the philosophers deny this possibility.

Key Terms
السببية
الاقتران
خرق العادات
التساوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is a purely accidental coincidence with no regularity.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali's critique establishes that causal relations are not necessary but habitual conjunctions created by God, thereby safeguarding divine omnipotence and the possibility of miracles.

Causality and Divine Omnipotence: Between Ash'ari Occasionalism and Quranic Laws
Critiques Ash'ari causality denial and presents Quranic reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the key objections to the Ash'ari denial of causality and explain the Quranic reconciliation.

Core Idea
Denying causality does not require denying regular natural laws; God's power encompasses both.

The debate between al-Ghazali and Ibn Rushd on causality is often misunderstood as a clash between occasionalism and naturalism. This passage critiques the Ash'ari assumption that causality implies polytheism, and instead offers a Quranic framework where God creates both causes and their effects while maintaining the regularity of natural laws—except when miracles occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central objection to the Ash'ari position
The Ash'aris assume that attributing any causal influence to natural causes leads to polytheism (shirk). The author counters that causality as a natural system does not conflict with divine power.
2
Understand the conciliatory response
All composite causes are created by God; their operation does not negate God's ability to intervene (transition from 'ada to khariq al-'ada).
3
Recognize al-Ghazali's actual position
He warns against self-causality that denies the First Cause, but he does not deny all causal regularity—he only rejects necessary connection.
4
See Ibn Rushd's agreement
Ibn Rushd also affirms that an external agent's action is a condition, not a replacement, for natural causes.
5
Grasp the Quranic synthesis
Laws (sunan) are constant but can be broken by divine will for miracles; this acknowledges both regularity and divine intervention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن الغزالي إذ ينكر مبدأ السببية أو العلية فإنه يحيل هذه الأسباب ومسبباتها جميعاً إلى الله - تعالى - ليجعله الفاعل الحقيقي لها. والحق أن أهم مأخذ يمكن أن يواجه به الأشاعرة – ومعهم الغزالي – يتمثل في افتراضهم أن القول بإسناد التأثير لتلك الأسباب ينتهي بنا إلى الشرك، لأن القول بمبدأ السببية يلزم منه القول بفاعلين حقيقيين، وذلك ليس صحيحاً، إذ القول بالسببية من حيث هي نظام طبيعي لا يصطدم بقدرة الله ومشيئته المطلقة، ويصبح - تبعاً لهذا - التسليم بأن الله خالق الأسباب ومسبباتها بدهية مباشرة. وكأن بعض الباحثين أدرك حقيقة الافتراق الذي أدى إليه الخلاف حول مسألة العلية هذه من حيث نزاع الباحثين العملي واسع الهوة فيها فسعى - في محاولة توفيقية - إلى أن يخفف من غلواء الجدل الذي دار بين الغزالي ومن يرى رأيه في نفي السببية مطلقاً - وإن كان ظاهر الأمر كذلك ـ أو اعتماد ابن رشد ومن يرى رأيه السببية فاعلاً كلياً - ولو لم يكن ثمة ما يقنع بذلك. إن الموقف الذي يجلي الغموض، ولعله أن يقرّب بين وجهات النظر حول الموضوع يكمن في تقرير أن جميع هذه الأسباب المركبة في الأشياء مخلوقة لخالق واحد هو الله - سبحانه وتعالى. وإن عملها في مسبباتها لا يعني انتفاء قدرة الموجد الأول الأوحد لها على إيقاف عملها، بل إنه سبحانه – شاء إخراج الأمر من (العادة) إلى (خارق العادة) لحكمة يريدها الله- سبحانه -. والغزالي لم يصنع أكثر من الحذر والتحذير من أن يكون الحديث عن علاقة الضرورة بين الأسباب والمسببات مضيفاً إلى القول بالسببية الذاتية التي تنكر السبب الأول، أو تنكر إمكان وجواز تدخله لنقض ((العادة))، وإيقاف عمل الأسباب في المسببات بواسطة أسباب أخرى غير عادية يوجدها الله - سبحانه وتعالى -. وذلك يعني إيمانه بالسببية ولكنه ينبه فقط على سببية لا يدركها ولا يسلّم بها الذين لا يؤمنون. وابن رشد لا يختلف في حقيقة الأمر مع الغزالي إذ ينص على أن فعل الموجودات ليس من بعضها في بعض، أو أنها مكتفية بأنفسها، بل يقر ابن رشد بأن ثمة فاعلاً خارجياً فعله شرط في فعلها ووجودها. وإذا كان هذا رأياً توفيقياً لا يسلّم له بإطلاق فإن هناك ما هو أكثر إثارة للنقاش في هذا السياق، وذلك هو الاتجاه الداعي إلى طي صفحة ذلك الخلاف فما عاد هناك ما يسوغ استدعاءه اليوم. فأسئلة من مثل هل النار تحرق أم أن الله - تعالى - هو الذي يحدث فيها الحرق؟ وهل السكين هي التي تقطع أم أن الله يحدث القطع فيها عند الجز ... إلخ؟ لا معنى لها، بل الذي يعنينا هو إدراك سنة الله تعالى أن جعل المادة القابلة للاحتراق تحترق حين تقع في النار، وأن يخلق الشبع عند تناول الطعام والشفاء مع الدواء، والإنبات عند توافر الشروط للبذرة. فهذه الصفات الخاصة بالمادة سواء صفة الذرة أو صفة مركباتها جميعها من صنع الله - تعالى - ومخلوقاته ذات السنن التي لا تتغير ولا تتبدل. والمنهج القرآني يعترف بفعل السنن والقوانين في المسببات المتولّدة عنها، ولكنه يؤكد في الوقت ذاته على أن هذه السنن أو القوانين شأنها شأن الظواهر الأخرى من حيث إنها جميعاً مخلوقة لله - تعالى - فهي وإن كانت تسير وفق نظام مطّرد ومحكم لكن ذلك لن ينسينا في أي لحظة أنها جزء من خلق الله، أو جزء من إرادته، حيث إذا شاءت إرادة الخالق المبدع خرق هذا الاطراد المعتاد لعمل هذه السنن، لإظهار معجزة الرسول، أو تحذير لأقوام أو أفراد لا يعترفون لله - تعالى - بالألوهية والربوبية، فإن ذلك القانون يتوقف أو يخرق لهذا الغرض مثلاً.
Al-Ghazali, when he denies the principle of causality or causation, refers all these causes and their effects to God - exalted - to make Him the true agent. The truth is that the most important objection that can be faced by the Ash'aris - including al-Ghazali - is their assumption that attributing influence to those causes leads us to polytheism, because asserting the principle of causality necessitates asserting two real agents, and that is not correct, since asserting causality as a natural system does not conflict with God's absolute power and will, and accordingly, the acknowledgment that God is the creator of causes and their effects becomes a direct intuition. And it is as if some researchers recognized the reality of the divergence that led to the disagreement on this issue of causality, given the vast practical gap in it, so they sought - in a conciliatory attempt - to mitigate the intensity of the debate that occurred between al-Ghazali and those who hold his view in denying causality absolutely - although the apparent matter is so - or the adoption of Ibn Rushd and those who hold his view of causality as a universal agent - even if there is nothing convincing about that. The position that clarifies the ambiguity, and perhaps brings viewpoints closer on the subject, lies in the assertion that all these composite causes in things are created by one Creator, God - glorified and exalted. And their action upon their effects does not negate the power of the first and only originator to stop their action; rather, He - glorified - willed to bring the matter from (habit) to (the miraculous) for a wisdom that God - glorified - desires. And al-Ghazali did nothing more than caution and warn that speaking about a necessary relationship between causes and effects might add to the assertion of self-causality that denies the first cause, or denies the possibility and permissibility of His intervention to break the (habit) and stop the action of causes upon effects through other extraordinary causes that God - glorified and exalted - creates. That means his belief in causality, but he only alerts to a causality that those who do not believe do not perceive or accept. Ibn Rushd does not differ in reality from al-Ghazali, as he states that the action of existents is not from some upon others, nor that they are self-sufficient; rather, Ibn Rushd affirms that there is an external agent whose action is a condition for their action and existence. If this is a conciliatory opinion that is not absolutely accepted, then there is something more debatable in this context, which is the trend calling for turning the page on that disagreement, as there is no longer any justification for invoking it today. Questions like: Does fire burn, or does God - exalted - create burning in it? Does the knife cut, or does God create the cutting in it at the moment of cutting? etc., have no meaning. Rather, what concerns us is realizing God's sunna that He made the combustible matter burn when it falls into fire, and that He creates satiety upon eating food, recovery with medicine, and sprouting when conditions are met for the seed. For these specific properties of matter, whether the property of the atom or the property of its compounds, are all from the making of God - exalted - and His creations with sunan that do not change or alter. The Quranic methodology recognizes the action of sunan and laws in the effects generated from them, but it simultaneously affirms that these sunan or laws, like other phenomena, are all created by God - exalted - so although they proceed according to a consistent and precise system, that will not make us forget for a moment that they are part of God's creation, or part of His will, such that if the will of the creative Creator wishes to break this familiar consistency in the operation of these sunan, to show a miracle of the Messenger, or a warning to peoples or individuals who do not acknowledge God - exalted - for divinity and lordship, then that law stops or is broken for that purpose, for example.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological and critical discussion of the Islamic debate on causality. It begins by stating al-Ghazali's position: he denies causality by referring all causes and effects directly to God as the only real agent. The author then presents a central objection to the Ash'ari (and al-Ghazali's) view: namely, that attributing any causal influence to natural causes is seen as polytheism because it implies multiple agents. The author counters that causality as a natural system does not conflict with God's power, and that acknowledging God as creator of causes and effects is intuitive. The passage then describes a conciliatory approach: all composite causes are created by God, and their operation does not negate God's ability to intervene, moving from 'habit' (customary course of events) to the 'miraculous'. Al-Ghazali is portrayed as merely warning against a self-causality that denies the first cause. Ibn Rushd is then cited as agreeing that existents are not self-sufficient but require an external agent. The author then argues that the debate is outdated because questions like 'Does fire burn?' are meaningless; instead, we should recognize that God has established sunan (laws) that govern phenomena such as burning, satiety, and growth, and these are constant but subject to miraculous interruption. Finally, the Quranic methodology is summarized: it affirms the operation of laws while emphasizing that they are created and can be broken by God's will for purposes like miracles.

Key Terms
السببية
العادة
خارق العادة
السنن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key to reconciling the views of al-Ghazali and Ibn Rushd?
A) Accepting that natural causes have independent power.
B) Recognizing that all composite causes are created by a single Creator who can suspend their action.
C) Denying that miracles exist.
D) Claiming that al-Ghazali and Ibn Rushd never disagreed.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic view of causality affirms God's creation and control over both causes and their regular effects, with the possibility of miraculous interruption.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Identify the logical fallacy in the Ash'ari claim that 'attributing causality to natural causes leads to shirk' as presented in the passage. Explain why the author considers this a misunderstanding.
