Desire and Memory: The Relativity of Reason
Everyday examples of memory bias

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how personal desires bias memory and reasoning in everyday intellectual tasks.

Core Idea
Your desires shape what you remember and how you reason.

We often think of reason as an objective faculty, but everyday experience shows that our desires influence what we recall and how we think. This lesson explores the relativity of reason through examples from education and child psychology, showing that even intelligent individuals are not immune to bias.

Guided Path
1
Identify the memory examples
The passage gives examples of a teacher who cannot recall a student's name or a book title, and a child who remembers a promise but forgets a chore. Notice how the teacher's desire to recall affects memory.
2
Recognize the selectivity of recall
The author states that individuals often recall only what they desire to recall. This is a key point about the relativity of reason—it is not purely objective.
3
Extend to reasoning
The same selectivity occurs in reasoning: people remember evidence supporting their beliefs more than contradicting evidence. This can lead to errors even in intelligent people.
4
Reflect on Islamic applications
Consider how this bias affects our understanding of religious texts or theological arguments. The Quran warns against following desires (hawa) without guidance from Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل. ومن خبرات الحياة اليومية - في مجال التعليم - التي تزيد من توضيح هذه النسبية في العقل ما يشير إليه أحد الباحثين من كون المدرس قد لا يستطيع استرجاع اسم تلميذ سابق، أو عنوان كتاب قرره في العام الماضي، أو المكان الذي أوقف فيه سيارته كما قد لا يستطيع استرجاع أشياء كثيرة مرت بخبرته سابقاً، ولذلك فإن الفرد قد لا يسترجع غالباً إلا الأشياء التي يرغب في استرجاعها. ومن الأمثلة على ذلك يقول هذا الباحث - : إن الطفل يتذكر بقوة أن أمه وعدته بأنها ستصحبه إلى السيرك يوم السبت، لكنه ينسى بسرعة أنها قد طلبت منه أن يشذب الحديقة، تماماً كما أن العالم قد يتذكر الأشياء التي تدعم معتقداته أكثر من غيرها. والأمر ذاته قد يحصل في التفكير والاستدلال حتى عند الأفراد شديدي الذكاء، وذلك إما لخطأ في التفكير والاستدلال، أو نتيجة لاستخدام لوسائل إحصائية وتجريبية غير مناسبة. وقد ينتج ذلك أيضاً لتحيّز انفعالي، كما هو الحاصل عند ذلك الطفل الذي تذکر بشدّة حقه في موعد أمه له، في حين نسى واجبه في تشذيب الحديقة، أو حتى لدى العالم الذي يتذكر ما يدعم معتقداته دون أن يولي الاهتمام ذاته لما يخالفها. وهذا ما كشفت عنه بعض الدراسات التجريبية الحديثة في علم النفس. فقد قدمت بعض البراهين القياسية إلى مجموعة من الطلبة، وطلب منهم تبيين مــا إذا كانت النتيجة منطقية من المقدمتين المستخدمتين في القياس. فتبين أن نصف البراهين القياسية -وهي متعلقة بأمور الحياة العادية - أقـل خطـأ لدى جميـع الطلبة، في حين وقعوا جميعاً في أخطاء في النصف المتعلق بالأمور التي من شأنها أن تثير الانفعال. وصدق الله: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَجِيبُوا لَكَ فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّمَا يَتَّبِعُونَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنِ اتَّبَعَ هَوَاهُ بِغَيْرِ هُدَى مِنْ اللَّهِ... [القصص: ٥٠/٢٨]. ونلاحظ أن الفخر الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤ هـ) قد تنبه إلى ذلك، وتوصل بقوة إدراكه وملاحظاته إلى هذه الحقيقة حين فسر قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِها أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹/۷]. فقد قال: إن الآية تشير إلى أن الإنسان إذا تأكدت نفرته عن شيء حتى صارت تلك النفرة المتأكدة الراسخة مانعة له عـــن فهم الكلام الدال على صحة الشيء، ومانعة عن إبصار محاسنه وفضائله، وهذه حالة وجدانية ضرورية يجدها كلّ عاقل من نفسه، ولهذا السبب قالوا في المثل المشهور: (حبّك الشيء يعمي ويصم).
Chapter Three: Second Section - Reason. From everyday life experiences - in the field of education - that further clarify this relativity in reason is what one researcher points out: that the teacher may not be able to recall the name of a previous student, or the title of a book he taught last year, or the place where he parked his car, and he may not be able to recall many things that passed through his experience before. Therefore, an individual often recalls only the things he desires to recall. Examples of this include the researcher saying: The child strongly remembers that his mother promised to take him to the circus on Saturday, but quickly forgets that she asked him to trim the garden, just as the scholar may remember things that support his beliefs more than others. The same thing can happen in thinking and reasoning even among highly intelligent individuals, either due to an error in thinking and reasoning, or as a result of using inappropriate statistical and experimental methods. This can also result from emotional bias, as is the case with that child who strongly remembered his right to his mother's appointment, while forgetting his duty to trim the garden, or even with the scholar who remembers what supports his beliefs without giving the same attention to what contradicts them. This is what some modern experimental studies in psychology have revealed. They presented some syllogistic proofs to a group of students and asked them to indicate whether the conclusion was logical from the two premises used in the syllogism. It turned out that half of the syllogistic proofs - which were related to everyday life matters - had fewer errors among all students, while they all made errors in the half related to matters that would arouse emotion. And Allah spoke the truth: {If they do not respond to you, then know that they follow their own desires. And who is more astray than one who follows his desire without guidance from Allah?} [Al-Qasas 28:50]. We note that Fakhr al-Razi (d. 604 AH) was aware of this and arrived at this truth through his strong perception and observations when he interpreted the verse: {And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. It is they who are the heedless.} [Al-A'raf 7:179]. He said: The verse indicates that when a person's aversion to something is confirmed so that this confirmed and firm aversion prevents him from understanding speech indicating the truth of the thing, and prevents him from seeing its merits and virtues, and this is an essential emotional state that every rational person finds in himself, and for this reason they said in the famous proverb: 'Your love of a thing blinds and deafens.'
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the relativity of reason and the impact of emotional bias on logical reasoning. The author begins by illustrating how memory is selective and influenced by desires, using everyday examples from education and child psychology. He then extends this to reasoning, noting that even intelligent individuals can err due to emotional bias or inappropriate methods. He supports this with a psychological study where students made more errors in syllogisms with emotionally charged content. The passage then invokes Quranic verses to underscore the danger of following desires, and cites Fakhr al-Razi's tafsir of Al-A'raf 7:179, where he explains that strong aversion can blind a person to the truth. The author concludes that this recognition of reason's relativity does not diminish its importance but rather informs its proper use in research and education.

الهوى
الانفعال

A) The teacher lacks intelligence.

C) The teacher has a memory disorder.
D) The student was not memorable.

Key Takeaway
Desire biases memory and reasoning, making reason relative rather than absolute in everyday situations.

Emotional Bias in Syllogistic Reasoning and Quranic Guidance
Psychological study on syllogisms and al-Razi's commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recognize how emotional bias can invalidate syllogistic reasoning and relate this to the Quranic warning against following desires.

Core Idea
Emotions can corrupt even the most logical syllogisms.

A psychological study showed that students made more errors in syllogisms with emotionally charged content. This lesson connects that finding to the Quranic condemnation of following desires and to Fakhr al-Razi's commentary on how aversion blinds the heart to truth.

Guided Path
1
Understand the experiment
Researchers presented students with syllogistic proofs (two premises and a conclusion) related to everyday life or emotionally charged topics. Students had to judge logical validity.
Syllogistic proofs are called al-barāhīn al-qiyāsiyya.
2
Compare error rates
Half the syllogisms were neutral, half were emotionally arousing. All students made more errors in the emotionally charged set, regardless of intelligence.
3
Connect to the Quranic verses
The author quotes Quran 28:50, which says those who do not respond to the truth follow their desires, and Quran 7:179, describing people with hearts that do not understand.
These verses show that emotional attachment (hawa) prevents proper reasoning.
4
Analyze al-Razi's commentary
Fakhr al-Razi explains that firm aversion (nufra) can prevent a person from understanding speech that indicates the truth, and from seeing its merits. This is a psychological insight centuries before modern studies.
Al-Razi's observation aligns with the proverb 'Love of something blinds and deafens.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل. ومن خبرات الحياة اليومية - في مجال التعليم - التي تزيد من توضيح هذه النسبية في العقل ما يشير إليه أحد الباحثين من كون المدرس قد لا يستطيع استرجاع اسم تلميذ سابق، أو عنوان كتاب قرره في العام الماضي، أو المكان الذي أوقف فيه سيارته كما قد لا يستطيع استرجاع أشياء كثيرة مرت بخبرته سابقاً، ولذلك فإن الفرد قد لا يسترجع غالباً إلا الأشياء التي يرغب في استرجاعها. ومن الأمثلة على ذلك يقول هذا الباحث - : إن الطفل يتذكر بقوة أن أمه وعدته بأنها ستصحبه إلى السيرك يوم السبت، لكنه ينسى بسرعة أنها قد طلبت منه أن يشذب الحديقة، تماماً كما أن العالم قد يتذكر الأشياء التي تدعم معتقداته أكثر من غيرها. والأمر ذاته قد يحصل في التفكير والاستدلال حتى عند الأفراد شديدي الذكاء، وذلك إما لخطأ في التفكير والاستدلال، أو نتيجة لاستخدام لوسائل إحصائية وتجريبية غير مناسبة. وقد ينتج ذلك أيضاً لتحيّز انفعالي، كما هو الحاصل عند ذلك الطفل الذي تذکر بشدّة حقه في موعد أمه له، في حين نسى واجبه في تشذيب الحديقة، أو حتى لدى العالم الذي يتذكر ما يدعم معتقداته دون أن يولي الاهتمام ذاته لما يخالفها. وهذا ما كشفت عنه بعض الدراسات التجريبية الحديثة في علم النفس. فقد قدمت بعض البراهين القياسية إلى مجموعة من الطلبة، وطلب منهم تبيين مــا إذا كانت النتيجة منطقية من المقدمتين المستخدمتين في القياس. فتبين أن نصف البراهين القياسية -وهي متعلقة بأمور الحياة العادية - أقـل خطـأ لدى جميـع الطلبة، في حين وقعوا جميعاً في أخطاء في النصف المتعلق بالأمور التي من شأنها أن تثير الانفعال. وصدق الله: ﴿فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَجِيبُوا لَكَ فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّمَا يَتَّبِعُونَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنِ اتَّبَعَ هَوَاهُ بِغَيْرِ هُدَى مِنْ اللَّهِ... [القصص: ٥٠/٢٨]. ونلاحظ أن الفخر الرازي (ت: ٦٠٤ هـ) قد تنبه إلى ذلك، وتوصل بقوة إدراكه وملاحظاته إلى هذه الحقيقة حين فسر قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيراً مِنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنْسِ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌ لا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌ لا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌ لا يَسْمَعُونَ بِها أُولَئِكَ كَالأَنْعامِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْغافِلُونَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹/۷]. فقد قال: إن الآية تشير إلى أن الإنسان إذا تأكدت نفرته عن شيء حتى صارت تلك النفرة المتأكدة الراسخة مانعة له عـــن فهم الكلام الدال على صحة الشيء، ومانعة عن إبصار محاسنه وفضائله، وهذه حالة وجدانية ضرورية يجدها كلّ عاقل من نفسه، ولهذا السبب قالوا في المثل المشهور: (حبّك الشيء يعمي ويصم).
Chapter Three: Second Section - Reason. From everyday life experiences - in the field of education - that further clarify this relativity in reason is what one researcher points out: that the teacher may not be able to recall the name of a previous student, or the title of a book he taught last year, or the place where he parked his car, and he may not be able to recall many things that passed through his experience before. Therefore, an individual often recalls only the things he desires to recall. Examples of this include the researcher saying: The child strongly remembers that his mother promised to take him to the circus on Saturday, but quickly forgets that she asked him to trim the garden, just as the scholar may remember things that support his beliefs more than others. The same thing can happen in thinking and reasoning even among highly intelligent individuals, either due to an error in thinking and reasoning, or as a result of using inappropriate statistical and experimental methods. This can also result from emotional bias, as is the case with that child who strongly remembered his right to his mother's appointment, while forgetting his duty to trim the garden, or even with the scholar who remembers what supports his beliefs without giving the same attention to what contradicts them. This is what some modern experimental studies in psychology have revealed. They presented some syllogistic proofs to a group of students and asked them to indicate whether the conclusion was logical from the two premises used in the syllogism. It turned out that half of the syllogistic proofs - which were related to everyday life matters - had fewer errors among all students, while they all made errors in the half related to matters that would arouse emotion. And Allah spoke the truth: {If they do not respond to you, then know that they follow their own desires. And who is more astray than one who follows his desire without guidance from Allah?} [Al-Qasas 28:50]. We note that Fakhr al-Razi (d. 604 AH) was aware of this and arrived at this truth through his strong perception and observations when he interpreted the verse: {And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind. They have hearts with which they do not understand, they have eyes with which they do not see, and they have ears with which they do not hear. Those are like livestock; rather, they are more astray. It is they who are the heedless.} [Al-A'raf 7:179]. He said: The verse indicates that when a person's aversion to something is confirmed so that this confirmed and firm aversion prevents him from understanding speech indicating the truth of the thing, and prevents him from seeing its merits and virtues, and this is an essential emotional state that every rational person finds in himself, and for this reason they said in the famous proverb: 'Your love of a thing blinds and deafens.'
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about the relativity of reason and the impact of emotional bias on logical reasoning. The author begins by illustrating how memory is selective and influenced by desires, using everyday examples from education and child psychology. He then extends this to reasoning, noting that even intelligent individuals can err due to emotional bias or inappropriate methods. He supports this with a psychological study where students made more errors in syllogisms with emotionally charged content. The passage then invokes Quranic verses to underscore the danger of following desires, and cites Fakhr al-Razi's tafsir of Al-A'raf 7:179, where he explains that strong aversion can blind a person to the truth. The author concludes that this recognition of reason's relativity does not diminish its importance but rather informs its proper use in research and education.

Key Terms
البراهين القياسية
الانفعال
الهوى
النفرة

A) Syllogisms about mathematics.
B) Syllogisms with emotionally neutral content.
C) Syllogisms that arouse emotion.
D) Syllogisms with many premises.

Key Takeaway
Emotional bias can undermine syllogistic reasoning, a fact recognized by both modern psychology and classical Islamic scholarship.

Then modify it to an emotionally charged topic (e.g., regarding a controversial fiqh issue) and explain how emotional bias might affect one's judgment of its validity.

Critique of Rationalist Overvaluation of Intellect
Author critiques the primacy of reason and argues for mutual dependence of intellect and senses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's arguments against the claim that intellectual knowledge is inherently more certain than sensory knowledge, and evaluate the evidence presented.

Core Idea
Intellect and senses are interdependent; neither alone produces certainty.

In this passage, the author challenges the common rationalist position that the intellect is the primary, superior source of knowledge. Instead, he argues that the intellect and senses function in a complementary, organic relationship. By examining his critique of an opposing argument based on a Quranic verse and his analysis of causality, you will learn to recognize the flaws in overvaluing one faculty over the other, a key skill in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rationalist claim being attacked
The author begins by stating the rationalist position: the intellect is the true active agent behind the senses, transforming sensations into real knowledge. He also refers to an opponent who argues that sensory knowledge is certain because hearing and sight are perfections of God (citing Quran 42:11).
The opponent's argument is that since these senses are divine attributes, their knowledge must be certain.
2
Analyze the author's refutation of the Quranic argument
The author questions the logical link: does being a perfection automatically make sensory knowledge certain? He points out that senses can deceive, and that intellectual processing is necessary for certainty. This reveals the fallacy of assuming that a noble source guarantees certain knowledge.
The author's rhetorical questions challenge the opponent's reasoning.
3
Examine the claim of interdependence
The author argues that the function between intellect and senses is complementary and organic. Even if humans are distinguished by intellect, the intellect cannot produce valuable knowledge without sensory input.
He distinguishes between innate intellectual knowledge and acquired knowledge that requires interaction with objects.
4
Understand the critique of causality as a primary law
The author uses causality as an example: although causality is a primary intellectual law, the intellect cannot link cause and effect without empirical observation. He illustrates with medicine and epidemics: we only know the connection after repeated observation.
This shows that even 'primary' intellectual laws depend on sensory experience.
5
Recognize the conclusion against absolute distinction
The author concludes that elevating intellect to produce certain knowledge is unjustified and merely echoes Greek and classical European thought. The Ghazalian analogy of heart (intellect) as ruler and senses as soldiers is used but modified to show systemic interdependence.
The heart-ruler analogy does not mean one acts without the other; it is a systemic relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الثاني - العقل
الباحثين - استنتاجاً من هذه الحقيقة - أن الدور الحقيقي الفاعل إنمـا هـو للعقل الذي يقف وراء الحواس، ويجعل من إحساساتها إدراكات ومعارف حقيقيـة تنقلها من الغرائز والانعكاسات التي تشترك فيها سائر الحيوانات المزودة بمثل تلك الحواس، بيد أنها لا تتعدى الاهتداء الغريزي. كما أن من غير المفهوم ما حاول به باحث آخر أن يردّ على هذا الرأي فراح يستشهد بقول الله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ليستدل من خلاله على أن وسيلتي السمع والبصر من الكمال، ولذلك فالمعارف الآتية من قبلهما بالنسبة للإنسان معارف يقينية مؤكدة. ولست أدري كيف تكون يقينية مؤكدة لمجرد أنهـا مـن صفـات الكمال عند الإنسان؟ فهل يرفع هذا التشريف معارفها إلى مقام المعارف اليقينية المؤكدة؟ وأين نذهب - إذن - بحقيقة خداع الحواس الذي قد يحصل أحياناً؟ وهل كانت ترقى هذه المعارف إلى اليقين - أحياناً - إن لم يكن العقل قد استقبلها وتفاعل معها؟
والقول بمنح العقل مزية جوهرية على الحواس إلى الحد الذي يشعرك بالميل نحو المذهب العقلاني لا يخلو من غلو. ذلك أن الوظيفة تكاملية بينهما، والعلاقة عضوية تبادلية بحيث نقول: إنه وإن صح تميّز الإنسان عن غيره بالعقل، لكنه لن يحيل أي معرفة يدركها العقل بقوانينه الأولية - عـدا مـا سـواها - إلى معارف حقيقية ذات قيمة لو لم تكن الحواس ومعطياتها قد منحت لـه منـافـذ الإدراك وإحداث عمليات التعقل العليا.
يجب التفريق بين نوعين من المعرفة العقلية:
١ - المعرفة الأولية الثابتة أو العقل الغريزي.
٢ - المعرفة المكتسبة التي يحصلها العقل نتيجة تفاعله مع الأشياء.
ولعلّ من أكثر الشواهد حضوراً في هذا الباب ما لاحظه أحد الباحثين من عدم وجود علاقة بين السبب والنتيجة عقلا - رغم أن السببية أحد أبرز قوانين العقل الأولية - على معنى أن العقل لا قدرة له على ربط الأسباب بالنتائج أو العكس إلا من خلال مشاهدة هذا الارتباط في الواقع الخارجي.
ونحن نلاحظ أيضاً أنه لا يوجد ارتباط بين الدواء وأثره عقلاً، وإلا كان بإمكان العقل فهم هذا السبب قبل مشاهدة النتيجة ولكن لما لم يحدث ذلك، وإنما يحدث رؤية الارتباط بينهما سلباً أو إيجاباً فقط فإن النتيجة توجد إذا وجد السبب، وتفقد إذا فقد. ولو أمكن للعقل أن يربط الأسباب بالنتائج لفهم الناس أسباب الوباء قبل أن يشاهدوها في الواقع، ولكن نتيجة لخبرات العقل الذي سبق أن شاهد أسبابها من قبل؛ حكم بأسباب الوباء بعد ذلك.
ومن طرائف الأمور تشبيه القلب (العقل) بالحاكم الذي يحتل مكان القيادة، وتشبيه الحواس بالجنود له وتصبح العلاقة بينهما القلب والحواس متجلية في السمع والتعقل الذي هو شأن من شؤون القلب. ومن قبل شبه الإمام الغزالي القلب بأن له جُنْدَين، أحدهما يرى بالأبصار والآخر لا يرى إلا بالبصائر. والقلب في حكم الملك والجنود في حكم الخدم والأعوان.
ولكن كون القلب بمثابة الحاكم والحواس بمثابة الجند فإن ذلك لا يعني قيام دور مقصود ومنظم لأحدهما من دون الآخر مطلقاً. ذلك لأن طبيعة عملهما قائمة وفق عملية نظامية يتأثر الكل فيها بالجزء والعكس بالعكس.
إذا تبين ذلك لم يعد هناك ما يسوّغ إعلاء قدر العقل لإظهار معارفه مظهر اليقينيات، لأن هذا الزعم يغدو ترديداً مقصوداً أو غير مقصود المقولات اليونانيين والأوربيين الكلاسيكيين حين فرّقوا بين معارف العقل ومعارف الحواس.
Chapter Three, Section Two: The Intellect. Researchers conclude from this fact that the real effective role is for the intellect that stands behind the senses, and makes from their sensations true perceptions and knowledge, transferring them from the instincts and reflexes that all animals equipped with such senses share, but they do not exceed instinctual guidance. Also incomprehensible is what another researcher attempted to refute this opinion, citing the words of God Almighty: 'Nothing is like Him, and He is the Hearing, the Seeing' to argue that the faculties of hearing and sight are perfections, and therefore the knowledge coming from them for humans is certain confirmed knowledge. But I do not know how they can be certain and confirmed simply because they are among the perfections of humans? Does this honor elevate their knowledge to the level of certain confirmed knowledge? Where then do we go with the fact that the senses sometimes deceive? And would this knowledge ever attain certainty - sometimes - if the intellect had not received it and interacted with it? The claim of granting the intellect an essential advantage over the senses to the extent that it inclines you toward the rationalist school is not free of exaggeration. That is because the function is complementary between them, and the relationship is organic and reciprocal, so we say: Even if it is true that humans are distinguished from others by intellect, it will not convert any knowledge that the intellect perceives with its primary laws - except what is other than that - into true valuable knowledge if the senses and their data had not provided it with the avenues of perception and the activation of higher intellectual processes. It is necessary to distinguish between two types of intellectual knowledge: 1. Primary fixed knowledge or instinctive intellect. 2. Acquired knowledge that the intellect obtains as a result of its interaction with things. Perhaps among the most present evidences in this chapter is what one researcher observed: the absence of a rational relationship between cause and effect - despite causality being one of the most prominent primary laws of the intellect - meaning that the intellect has no ability to link causes to effects or vice versa except through observing this connection in external reality. We also note that there is no rational connection between medicine and its effect; otherwise the intellect would be able to understand this cause before observing the result, but since this does not happen, and only the observation of the connection between them negatively or positively occurs, the result exists if the cause exists and is lost if it is lost. If the intellect could link causes to effects, people would understand the causes of an epidemic before they observed them in reality, but as a result of the experiences of the intellect that had previously observed its causes, it judges the causes of the epidemic afterwards. Among the amusing things is the analogy of the heart (intellect) to a ruler who occupies the place of leadership, and the senses to soldiers, and the relationship between them, the heart and the senses, becomes evident in hearing and reasoning which is a matter of the heart. Previously, Imam al-Ghazali likened the heart as having two armies, one that sees with eyesight and the other that sees only with insight. The heart is in the position of a king and the soldiers are in the position of servants and aides. But the heart being like a ruler and the senses like soldiers does not mean that a deliberate and organized role is played by one without the other at all. That is because the nature of their work is based on a systematic process in which the whole is affected by the part and vice versa. If this is established, there is no longer any justification for elevating the intellect to present its knowledge as certainties, because this claim becomes a deliberate or unintentional repetition of the statements of the Greeks and classical Europeans when they distinguished between intellectual knowledge and sensory knowledge.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion critiquing the overvaluation of the intellect ('aql) over the senses (hawas) in knowledge acquisition. The author begins by stating the common claim that the intellect is the true active agent behind the senses, transforming sensations into real knowledge, unlike animals which only have instinct. The author then refutes an opposing argument that uses a Quranic verse (42:11) to claim that sensory knowledge is certain because hearing and sight are divine attributes. The author questions this reasoning, pointing out that senses can deceive and that certainty requires intellectual processing. Next, the author argues that granting the intellect an absolute advantage is exaggerated; the relationship is complementary and organic. The intellect cannot produce valuable knowledge without sensory input. The passage then distinguishes between two types of intellectual knowledge: innate (primary fixed) and acquired (from interaction with objects). A key example is causality: the intellect cannot rationally connect cause and effect without experiential observation, as seen in medicine and epidemics. The author uses analogies from Ghazali: the heart (intellect) is like a ruler and the senses like soldiers, but this does not mean one acts without the other; they function systematically. The conclusion is that elevating intellect to produce certain knowledge is unjustified and merely echoes Greek and classical European thought. All examples are rooted in Islamic epistemology and critique of rationalism.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): the intellectual faculty that processes sensory data and produces knowledge, distinct from instinct. The author distinguishes between innate (gharizi) and acquired intellectual knowledge.
الحواس (al-hawas): the five external senses that provide raw data to the intellect. The author emphasizes their necessity but also their potential deception.
السببية (al-sababiyya): causality as a primary intellectual law, but the intellect cannot establish causal connections without empirical observation.
المعرفة اليقينية (al-ma'rifa al-yaqiniyya): certain knowledge; the author denies that either intellect or senses alone yields certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author reject the claim that sensory knowledge is automatically certain because hearing and sight are perfections of God?
A) Because the senses are not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because even if they are perfections, senses can deceive and require intellectual processing
C) Because the intellect is superior and senses are irrelevant
D) Because only the heart can attain certainty

Key Takeaway
The author demonstrates that a rationalist overvaluation of the intellect is flawed because intellect and senses are interdependent; neither alone can produce certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a passage in al-Ghazali's 'Tahafut al-Falasifa' where he argues that philosophers' rational proofs for the eternity of the world are flawed. Identify which of their claims rely on assumptions that mix intellect and sensory experience. Explain how al-Ghazali's critique mirrors the interdependence argument from this lesson.
?
Analyze a contemporary debate in Islamic bioethics (e.g., the use of artificial intelligence in medical diagnosis). Using the author's criteria, evaluate whether the claim that 'AI provides certain knowledge' is justified, considering both sensory input (data) and intellectual processing (algorithms).

The Certainty of Revelation as a Source of Knowledge
Author establishes revelation's certainty via tawatur and its transcendence over sense and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the epistemological basis of revelation's certainty and distinguish it from sense and reason.

Core Idea
Revelation is certain, known via tawatur, and transcends sense and reason.

In this passage, the author establishes that revelation is not just a subjective experience but a certain source of knowledge. It is transmitted through tawatur (massive uninterrupted chains), which guarantees its epistemic reliability. Unlike sensory or rational knowledge, revelation stands above them, providing access to the unseen world. Let's examine how the author builds this case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of revelation's certainty
Find the phrase that explains how we know revelation is real: 'through the certain report that reached us by tawatur.' This is the epistemological grounding.
Tawatur is a concept from hadith sciences; here it's used for the fact of revelation itself.
2
Contrast revelation with sense and reason
The text says revelation 'transcends sense, intellect, and subjective spiritual doctrines.' Note the threefold distinction. Revelation is not validated by sense or reason; it is a higher epistemic tier.
3
Understand the role of tawatur
Realize that tawatur gives certainty to the historical occurrence of revelation. Without this transmission, we could not be certain that the Prophet received revelation.
This is similar to how we know the Quran text itself is authentic.
4
Apply to the Islamic education context
The author argues that revelation must be the absolute reference ('absolute reference') for judging phenomena. This is because it provides certainty that sense and reason cannot surpass.

الباب الثالث: الفصل الثالث - الوحي
وحيث إن احتواءه على المعطيات العلمية المدروسة في عصرنا تبدو كأنها تتحدى أي تفسير وضعي.
عقيمة حقاً المحاولات التي تسعى لإيجاد تفسير القرآن بالاعتماد فقط على الاعتبارات المادية)) (۱).
وهنا يتحتم على التربية الإسلامية اعتماد الوحي مصدراً وطريقة ذات مرجعية مطلقة في الحكم على الأحداث والظواهر والأشياء، وبلورة ذلك في إطار المنهج بمختلف عناصره. وحينئذ تكتسب التربية الإسلامية صفة الربانية بحق.
طريق معرفة الوحي
ونحن نفهم حقيقة الوحي في حياة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن طريق الخبر اليقيني الذي وصل إلينا بالتواتر طبقاً للشرط المعروف هنا وهو أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد أوحي إليه فعلاً (۲).
ومن المعلوم أن طريقة الوحي تختلف عن طرق الاتصال الحسي أو المدركات العقلية، وهذا الطريق - بحدّ ذاته - في المعرفة يقيني يتعالى على الحس والعقل والمذاهب الروحية الذاتية للإنسان حتى بعد بلوغه قمة مرتبة الولاية (۳).
أما دور العقل فينتهي عند التسليم بميدان عالم الغيب دون الدخول في كنهه أو حقيقته لأنه لا يقع تحت سلطانه، كمالا يقع تحت سلطان الحس والتجربة، أو خروجه عن قوانين إدراك طبيعة عالم الغيب وماهيته، لا أنهما يحكمان مخالفته للحس والتجربة، أو خروجه عن قوانين العقل الأولية(4). لأن أساس الوحي عرف بمقدمات راجعة إلى الحس والمشاهدة في عالم الشهادة، فأقرها العقل ووثق بها. وكذلك فإن التفكير العقلي هو المؤدي إلى حقيقة الإيمان بالغيب، وهو الذي أوصل الإنسان إلى المعرفة العلمية، بعكس التفكير الخرافي الذي يقوم على الجحود والإنكار لقواعد العقل(۱).
إن عالم الغيب وما يتضمنه من المبادئ التي لا قدرة للعقل والحواس وحدها على الاستقلال بإدراكها ليست خارج نطاق موضوعات سبل الوعي والمعرفة في المنهج الإسلامي، ذلك أن سبيلها هو الوحي، لخروجها عن عالم الشهادة الذي يمكن إدراكه بالحواس مثلاً (۲).
وقد رد الإمام الغزالي (ت: (٥٠٥هـ) على من لم يؤمن بظاهرة الوحي مدعياً أن الحس والعقل لا يدلان عليها بقوله : ووراء العقل طور آخر تفتح فيه أعين أخرى يبصر بها الغيب ، وما سيكون في المستقبل، وأمور أخر العقل معزول عنها كعزل قوة التمييز عن إدراك المعقولات وكعزل قوة الحس عن مدركات التمييز. وكما أن المميز لو عرضت عليه مدركات العقل لأباها واستبعدها، فكذلك بعض العقلاء أبوا مدركات النبوة واستبعدوها، وذلك عين الجهل، إذ لا مستند لهم إلا أنه طور لم يبلغه، ولم يوجد في حقه، فيظن أنه غير موجود في نفسه. والأكمه لو لم يعلم بالتواتر والتسامع الألوان والأشكال، وحكى له ذلك ابتداءً لم يفهمها، ولم يقربها. وقد قرب الله تعالى على خلقه بأن أعطاهم نموذجاً من خاصية النبوة، وهي النوم، إذ النائم يدركه ما سيكون من الغيب، إما صريحاً وإما في كسوة مثال يكشف عنه التعبير. هذا لو لم يجد به الإنسان من نفسه، وقيل له: إن من الناس من يسقط مغشياً عليه، كالميت ويزول عنه إحساسه وسمعه وبصره، فيدرك الغيب لأنكره، وأقام البرهان على
Chapter Three: Section Three - Revelation. Since its inclusion of scientific data studied in our time appears to challenge any positivist interpretation. Truly futile are the attempts that seek to interpret the Quran relying only on material considerations (1). Here Islamic education must adopt revelation as a source and method with absolute reference in judging events, phenomena, and things, and crystallize that within the framework of the methodology with its various elements. Then Islamic education acquires the quality of being divine rightly. The way of knowing revelation. We understand the reality of revelation in the life of the Prophet, peace be upon him, through the certain report that reached us by tawatur according to the known condition here that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was indeed inspired (2). It is known that the method of revelation differs from the methods of sensory contact or intellectual perceptions, and this path—in itself—in knowledge is certain, transcending sense, intellect, and the subjective spiritual doctrines of man even after reaching the peak of the station of sainthood (3). As for the role of reason, it ends at submission to the domain of the unseen world without entering into its essence or reality because it is not under its authority, just as it is not under the authority of sense and experience, or its departure from the laws of understanding the nature of the unseen world and its essence, not that they judge its contradiction to sense and experience, or its departure from the primary laws of reason (4). Because the basis of revelation is known by premises that go back to sense and observation in the world of testimony, so reason affirmed them and trusted them. Likewise, intellectual thinking is what leads to the truth of belief in the unseen, and it is what brought man to scientific knowledge, contrary to superstitious thinking that is based on denial and rejection of the rules of reason (1). The unseen world and what it contains of principles that reason and senses alone are incapable of independently perceiving are not outside the scope of the subjects of the means of consciousness and knowledge in the Islamic methodology; indeed, their means is revelation, because they are outside the world of testimony that can be perceived by the senses, for example (2). Imam al-Ghazali (d. 505 AH) replied to those who did not believe in the phenomenon of revelation, claiming that sense and reason do not indicate it, by saying: 'Beyond reason there is another stage in which other eyes open, seeing the unseen, what will be in the future, and other matters from which reason is isolated, like the isolation of the faculty of discrimination from perceiving intelligibles, and like the isolation of the sense from the perceptions of discrimination. Just as if the discriminator were presented with the perceptions of reason, he would reject them and consider them far-fetched, so too some rationalists rejected the perceptions of prophethood and considered them far-fetched, and that is pure ignorance, for they have no basis except that it is a stage they did not reach and did not occur in their case, so they think it does not exist in itself. And a blind man, if he did not know colors and shapes through tawatur and hearsay, and it was described to him initially, he would not understand them nor accept them. God, the Exalted, has made it easy for His creation by giving them a model of the property of prophethood, which is sleep, for the sleeper perceives what will be of the unseen, either explicitly or in a garment of an example whose interpretation reveals it. If a person did not find this from himself, and it was said to him: Some people fall unconscious, like a dead person, and their sensation, hearing, and sight disappear, and they perceive the unseen, he would deny it and would have argued for!'
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion on the status of revelation (wahy) as a source of knowledge in Islam. It begins by asserting that the Quran contains scientific data that challenge any purely materialistic interpretation, thus establishing revelation's superiority over sense-based science. The author then argues that Islamic education must adopt revelation as an absolute reference, giving it a divine character. The 'way of knowing revelation' is through certain report transmitted via tawatur (massive, unbroken chains), verifying that the Prophet indeed received revelation. Unlike sensory or intellectual means, this path transcends them and is certain. Reason's role is limited: it affirms the premises of revelation (based on observation in the visible world) and then submits to the unseen realm. The author clarifies that the unseen is not outside the scope of Islamic knowledge; its specific means is revelation. Finally, al-Ghazali is quoted to rebut those who deny revelation because sense and reason cannot perceive it. He uses analogies: like the blind man who cannot conceive colors, a person who has not experienced the prophetic stage cannot judge its reality. Sleep is given as a model, where one perceives the unseen without sensory input. The quote emphasizes that rejecting what one has not experienced is pure ignorance.

Key Terms
الوحي
التواتر
العقل
عالم الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do we know that the Prophet actually received revelation?
A) Through rational deduction
B) Through sensory experience
C) Through the certain report transmitted by tawatur
D) Through spiritual contemplation

Key Takeaway
Revelation is a certain source of knowledge, known via tawatur, and it transcends the domains of sense and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct an argument that uses tawatur to prove the fact of revelation to a skeptic, following the passage's logic.
?
Compare the certainty of revelation with the certainty of a mathematical proof. How does the passage differentiate them?

Commentary Notes
intermediate
7 min
The Role of Reason in Relation to Revelation
Author explains the limited role of reason and quotes Al-Ghazali's defense of revelation against rationalist objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the proper role of reason regarding the unseen world and how Al-Ghazali's analogy defends revelatory knowledge.

Core Idea
Reason affirms revelation's premises and submits to the unseen, beyond which it cannot go.

The passage clarifies that reason is not opposed to revelation; rather, reason has a specific, limited role. It affirms the premises that lead to belief in the unseen, but then it must submit to the unseen world, unable to penetrate its essence. Al-Ghazali strengthens this point with a powerful analogy comparing those who deny revelation to a blind person who denies colors. Let's unpack that.

Guided Path
1
Locate the role of reason
Find the sentence: 'أما دور العقل فينتهي عند التسليم بميدان عالم الغيب دون الدخول في كنهه' (the role of reason ends at submission to the unseen, not entering its essence). This is the key.
2
Understand reason's positive function
The passage also says reason affirms the premises of revelation based on sense and observation in the visible world. So reason is not passive; it plays a role in building the case for faith.
This avoids fideism: reason is engaged.
3
Analyze Al-Ghazali's analogy
Al-Ghazali says: just as a blind man cannot understand colors through reason alone, a person who has not experienced the prophetic faculty cannot judge its reality. Sleep is a model where one perceives the unseen without senses.
This is an analogical argument (tamthil) to show the limits of reason.
4
Extract the epistemological principle
The unseen world is known only through revelation, not because it is irrational, but because it is beyond the domain of human faculties. Reason must submit, not deny.

The Principle of Non-Contradiction between Reason and Revelation
Ibn Rushd establishes the principle that reason and revelation cannot conflict; apparent contradictions require interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Ibn Rushd's rule of ta'wil to reconcile apparent conflicts between rational demonstration and scriptural texts.

Core Idea
Truth does not oppose truth – reason and revelation are in harmony when properly understood.

Ibn Rushd (Averroes) articulated a foundational principle for Islamic epistemology: demonstrative reasoning (burhan) and revelation (shari'a) cannot ultimately conflict. Any apparent contradiction must be resolved by interpreting the scriptural text (ta'wil) according to linguistic rules. This lesson unpacks that principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Locate Ibn Rushd's central claim
Find the sentence where Ibn Rushd states that truth does not oppose truth: 'الحق لا يضاد الحق، بل يوافقه ويشهد له' (truth does not contradict truth, rather it agrees with and testifies for it). This is the foundation of his epistemology.
This claim presupposes that both reason and revelation are sources of certain truth.
2
Identify the condition for ta'wil
Note that ta'wil is required only when a demonstrative proof (burhan) reaches a conclusion that contradicts the apparent meaning (zahir) of revelation. Ibn Rushd says: 'كل ما أدى إليه البرهان وخالفه ظاهر الشرع، أن ذلك الظاهر يقبل التأويل'.
The burhan must be certain (qat'i) for ta'wil to be invoked.
3
Examine the linguistic requirement
The ta'wil must follow the 'Arab law of interpretation' – meaning it must be consistent with Arabic language usage. It is not arbitrary allegorization.
This restricts interpretations to those supported by linguistic principles and the overall context of revelation.
4
Distinguish levels of certainty
Understand that Ibn Rushd prioritizes reason only when it provides certainty (qat'i). If the rational evidence is speculative (zanni), the apparent meaning of revelation takes precedence. The commentator clarifies this to avoid misunderstanding.
This answers the criticism that Ibn Rushd unconditionally subordinates revelation to reason.
5
Apply to a sample contradiction
Consider a rational proof for the temporality of the world (huduth) versus a verse that says 'He is the First' (al-Awwal). A plausible ta'wil is that 'First' means priority in essence, not time. This shows how the rule works in practice.
Actual ta'wil may require consulting the entire Qur'an and Sunnah, as Ibn Rushd mentions.

من غير حرج يقول: وإذا تقرر هذا كله وكنا نعتقد – معشر المسلمين – أن شريعتنا هذه الإلهية، حق وأنها التي نبهت على هذه السعادة، ودعت إليها، التي هي المعرفة بالله عز وجل و مخلوقاته وأن ذلك متقرر عند كل مسلم من الطريق الذي اقتضته جبلته وطبيعته من التصديق، وذلك أن طباع الناس متفاضلة في التصديق، فمنهم من يصدق بالبرهان ومنهم من يصدق بالأقاويل الجدلية تصديق صاحب البرهان بالبرهان، إذ ليس في طباعه أكثر من ذلك، ومنهم من يصدق بالأقاويل الخطابية كتصديق صاحب البرهان بالأقاويل البرهانية (١). وقال: (وإذا كانت هذه الشريعة داعية إلى النظر المؤدي إلى معرفة الحق، فإنا معشر المسلمين نعلم على القطع أنه لا يؤدي النظر البرهاني إلى مخالفة ما ورد به الشرع، فإن الحق لا يضاد الحق، بل يوافقه ويشهد له (٢). ويؤكد على عدم التعارض بين الحكمة (الفلسفة أو العقل) والشريعة (الوحي) عند حديثه عن قانون التأويل، فيقول: (وإذا كان الفقيه يفعل هذا في كثير من الأحكام الشرعية (يقصد إعمال قانون التأويل) فكم بالحري أن يفعل ذلك صاحب علم البرهان فإن الحقيقة إنما عنده قياس ظني، والعارف عنده قياس يقيني. ونحن نقطع قطعاً أن كل ما أدى إليه البرهان وخالفه ظاهر الشرع، أن ذلك الظاهر يقبل التأويل على قانون التأويل العربي. وهذه القضية لا يشك فيها مسلم ولا يرتاب بها مؤمن. وما أعظم اليقين بها عند من زاول هذا المعنى وجربه وقصد هذا المقصد من الجمع بين المعقول والمنقول. بل نقول إنه ما من منطوق به في الشرع مخالف بظاهره لما أدى إليه البرهان إلا إذا اعتبر الشرع وتصفحت سائر أجزائه وجد في ألفاظ الشرع ما يشهد بظاهره لذلك التأويل، أو يقارب أن يشهد (١). ولخص أمر عدم التعارض هذا الشاطبي (ت: ٧٩٠هـ) بعبارة موجزة فقال: الأدلة الشرعية لا تنافي العقول (٣). ويرى أحد الباحثين في هذا الإطار أن غاية ما يستدل به علماء الكلام لا يخرج - عند التحقيق عن كون القرآن الكريم أقر للعقل بنظرته كمنـزع مشروع في الاجتهاد، بل إنه يشجع على ذلك، بيد أن القرآن الكريم لا يقر دعوی استقلال العقل عن مصدر المعرفة الإلهية وهو الوحي. وأخال جميع العبارات المتقدمة لأبرز رموز المدارس الفكرية الإسلامية لا تخرج عن هذا المعنى الأخير إلا ما قد يتبادر لأول مرة من الإلباس في قول ابن رشد: "ونحن نقطع قطعاً أن كلّ ما أدى إليه البرهان أن ذلك الظاهر يقبل التأويل على قانون التأويل (العربي)" فلربما يشعر هذا بأن ابن رشد يقدم العقل على السمع، وذلك - في حقيقة الأمر - مقيد بحالة الظن الظاهري ليس أكثر. وابن تيمية لم ينازع في هذا، وإنما رفض بشدة تقديم القطعي لكونه عقلياً لا لكونه قطعياً، واعتبار العقل أصل السمع. ومن هنا فإذا اتفق على أن العقلي قطعي فيقدم العقلي القطعي، وكذلك يقال في النقل لقطعيته. ومن جهة أخرى فإن ابن رشد ما زاد على أن أعمل قانون التأويل الذي يهدف إلى الجمع والتوفيق بين النقل والعقل لا أنـه يـردّ النصوص ولا يعترف بصحتها أو نسبتها إلى الشارع بدافع العجز أو الهـوى والتشهي كما يسارع بعض المتعجلين ممن لم ترسخ أقدامهم في معرفة الشريعة إن سلمنا برسوخها في معرفة الحكمة - إلى الرجم بذلك.
He says without difficulty: When all this is established, and we – the community of Muslims – believe that this divine shari'a of ours is the truth and that it has alerted to this happiness and called to it, which is knowledge of Allah Almighty and His creations, and that is established for every Muslim through the path that his innate disposition and nature necessitated of assenting, for indeed the natures of people vary in assent: among them are those who assent through demonstration and among them are those who assent through dialectical discourses just as the possessor of demonstration assents through demonstration, since his nature does not allow more than that, and among them are those who assent through rhetorical discourses just as the possessor of demonstration assents through demonstrative discourses (1). He said: And since this shari'a calls to reflection that leads to knowledge of the truth, we Muslims know with certainty that demonstrative reflection does not lead to contradicting what the shari'a has brought, for truth does not oppose truth, rather it agrees with and testifies for it (2). He emphasizes the non-contradiction between wisdom (philosophy or reason) and shari'a (revelation) when discussing the law of interpretation, saying: If the jurist does this in many legal rulings (i.e., applying the law of interpretation), how much more should the possessor of the science of demonstration do so, for indeed the ordinary person only has speculative reasoning, while the knower has certain reasoning. And we assert with absolute certainty that everything to which demonstration leads and which contradicts the apparent meaning of the shari'a, that apparent meaning is subject to interpretation according to the Arab law of interpretation. This proposition no Muslim doubts and no believer is skeptical about. How great is the certainty about it for one who has practiced this meaning and experienced it and intended this goal of reconciling the rational and the transmitted. Rather we say: There is no utterance in the shari'a whose apparent meaning contradicts what demonstration leads to, except that when the shari'a is considered and its various parts are examined, one finds in the expressions of the shari'a what apparently testifies to that interpretation, or nearly testifies (1). Al-Shatibi (d. 790 AH) summarized this matter of non-contradiction in a brief expression, saying: Legal proofs do not contradict rational proofs (3). One researcher in this context holds that the utmost of what the theologians use as evidence does not exceed – upon investigation – the fact that the Noble Qur'an affirmed for reason its view as a legitimate approach in ijtihad, rather it encourages that, but the Noble Qur'an does not affirm the claim of the independence of reason from the source of divine knowledge, which is revelation. And I think all the preceding statements of the most prominent figures of Islamic intellectual schools do not go beyond this last meaning except what might initially appear as ambiguity in Ibn Rushd's saying: "And we assert with absolute certainty that everything to which demonstration leads, that apparent meaning is subject to interpretation according to the Arab law of interpretation." Perhaps this suggests that Ibn Rushd prioritizes reason over revelation, but that – in reality – is restricted to a state of mere apparent opinion, nothing more. And Ibn Taymiyya did not dispute this; rather he vehemently rejected prioritizing the certain because it is rational, not because it is certain, and considering reason as the foundation of revelation. Hence if it is agreed that the rational is certain, then the certain rational is given priority, and likewise it is said regarding the transmitted for its certainty. On another hand, Ibn Rushd did nothing more than apply the law of interpretation, which aims at reconciling and harmonizing revelation and reason, not that he rejects the texts or denies their authenticity or their attribution to the Lawgiver out of incapacity or whimsical desire as some hasty people whose feet are not firmly rooted in knowledge of the shari'a – if we concede that they are firmly rooted in knowledge of wisdom – rush to accuse.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument establishing the principle of non-contradiction between reason and revelation. The author first quotes Ibn Rushd from 'Fasl al-Maqal' stating that demonstrative reasoning cannot contradict the truth of revelation because truth does not oppose truth. Ibn Rushd then introduces the law of interpretation (ta'wil): when a rational demonstration definitively shows something contrary to the apparent meaning of a scriptural text, that apparent meaning must be interpreted metaphorically according to the rules of Arabic language. He emphasizes that this principle is universally accepted among Muslims. The author then cites al-Shatibi's concise formulation: 'Legal proofs do not contradict rational proofs.' Following this, the author addresses a potential misunderstanding: Ibn Rushd's statement might be seen as prioritizing reason over revelation, but this is only when the rational proof is certain (qat'i); otherwise, the apparent meaning of revelation takes precedence. Ibn Taymiyya's objection was not to this principle but to the notion that reason is inherently prior to revelation. The passage concludes that Ibn Rushd's aim was harmonization, not rejection of revelation. The commentary should note that this discussion is central to Islamic epistemology, balancing the roles of 'aql and naql.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Rushd, when should a Muslim interpret the apparent meaning of a revelation (ta'wil)?
A) Whenever reason suggests a different possibility, even if it is uncertain
B) Only when a certain rational demonstration (burhan) contradicts the apparent meaning
C) Never, because revelation always overrides reason
D) Only for legal verses, not theological ones

Key Takeaway
Ibn Rushd's rule of ta'wil ensures that reason and revelation, both being sources of truth, cannot ultimately conflict.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given a rational proof that the universe is temporally originated (huduth), and the verse 'He is the First' (al-Awwal), use Ibn Rushd's rule to determine whether ta'wil is needed and propose a plausible interpretation.
?
Identify a case from Islamic theology (e.g., divine attributes like 'hand of Allah') where an apparent conflict between reason and revelation was resolved through ta'wil, and explain which condition of Ibn Rushd's rule applies.
